                <!-------------------------------------------><div class="typography">
<div class="fs-row">
<div class="fs-cell fs-lg-8">

<div class="sidebar-links collapsible-accordian">
  <div class="panel-group prevent-first-opening" id="collapse-accordion" role="tablist" aria-multiselectable="false">
    
    <!-- navigation object : Collapsible Accordion Content (2) --><!-- WYSIWYG - wrap all WYSIWYG text areas in `.typography` -->
<div class="typography">
<div class="fs-row">
<div class="fs-cell fs-lg-8">


  <p style="text-align: center;"><a href="#a">A</a> | <a href="#b">B</a> | <a href="#c">C</a> | <a href="#d">D</a> | <a href="#e">E</a> | <a href="#f">F</a> | <a href="#g">G</a> | <a href="#h">H</a> | <a href="#i">I</a> | J | K | <a href="#l">L</a> | <a href="#m">M</a> | <a href="#n">N</a> | <a href="#o">O</a> | <a href="#p">P</a> | Q | <a href="#r">R</a> | <a href="#s">S</a> | <a href="#t">T</a> | <a href="#u">U</a> | <a href="#v">V</a> | <a href="#w">W</a> | X | Y | Z<a id="up"></a><strong><br /></strong></p>
<h3><strong><a id="a"></a>A</strong></h3></div>

</div>
</div>
<div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#22" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="22">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="2">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          ACADEMIC DIFFICULTY - Warning and Formal Probation
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="22" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="2">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">The College endeavors to help students avoid academic difficulty. &nbsp;Historically, the most successful students attend class regularly, complete and submit assignments in a timely fashion, and seek assistance from instructors, advisors, Student Health Services, or the Academic Resource Center at the first signs of trouble. &nbsp;Moreover, students who are successful academically have learned to balance extracurricular activities with academics.</p>
<p align="justify">Academic&nbsp;performance is monitored closely by the Dean of Academic Life each term. &nbsp;The Dean will contact students at the conclusion of each term whose academic performance indicates a cause for concern.</p>
<p align="justify"><strong>Academic Warning&nbsp;</strong>may be triggered by any&nbsp;combination of two or more failing grades, incomplete grades, unsatisfactory grades, or course withdrawals in a term; a term grade point average below 1.80; or a cumulative grade point average less than the standards described in the table that follows.</p>
<p align="justify">Formal <strong>academic probation</strong> indicates that the quality of the student's work is below the level that might reasonably be expected to lead to graduation. &nbsp;A term grade point average below 1.00 or a cumulative grade point average less than the standards described below identify those students eligible for formal probation. &nbsp;All student performance indicating eligibility for formal probation will be reviewed by the Dean of Academic Life. &nbsp;After the review has been completed, students experiencing the most serious academic difficulties will be placed on formal probation. &nbsp;Student progress during the probationary period &nbsp;will &nbsp;be &nbsp;carefully &nbsp;examined. &nbsp;</p>
<p align="justify">At any time during the period, typically no more than two terms, the College can elect to remove the student from probation, continue the student on probation, or dismiss the student from Muhlenberg. &nbsp;Furthermore, students on formal probation seeking to enroll additional courses beyond what is considered a "normal load", either at Muhlenberg or elsewhere, are permitted to do so only at the discretion of the Dean of Academic Life; this provision includes enrollment in any type of summer term.</p>
<p align="justify">Cumulative academic performance is gauged on the number of course units <em><span class="italic">attempted </span></em> at Muhlenberg plus any transferred course units. &nbsp;Cumulative grade point averages less than the standards described in the table indicate the specific level of academic difficulty.</p>
<div class="center">
<table class="table border" style="border: 1px solid #000000; width: 100%;" border="1" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0">
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>
<p align="center"><strong> Attempted Course Units </strong></p>
</td>
<td>
<p class="center" style="text-align: center;"><strong>Academic Probation <br> or Suspension</strong></p>
</td>
<td>
<p align="center"><strong>Academic Warning</strong></p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
<p>5 or less</p>
</td>
<td>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp; Less than 1.50</p>
</td>
<td>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Less than 1.80</p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>&nbsp;</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
<p align="center"><strong> Attempted Course Units </strong></p>
</td>
<td>
<p align="center"><strong>Academic Probation</strong></p>
</td>
<td>
<p align="center"><strong>Academic Warning</strong></p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
<p>5.25 through 10</p>
</td>
<td>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp; Less than 1.80</p>
</td>
<td>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Less than 2.00</p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
<p>More than 10</p>
</td>
<td>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp; Less than 2.00</p>
</td>
<td>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</div>
<p align="justify">Finally, the College takes the position that any student permitted to enroll should be allowed to judge the wisdom of participating in extracurricular activities. &nbsp;Accordingly, a student experiencing academic difficulty may participate in such activities. &nbsp;Any student receiving an academic warning or placed on formal probation, however, is urged to give thoughtful consideration, in consultation with his or her academic advisor, to the structure of the total College program, curricular and extracurricular. &nbsp;(Contact the Dean of Academic Life with any questions.)</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#32" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="32">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="3">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          ACADEMIC DISMISSAL AND SUSPENSION
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="32" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="3">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Muhlenberg College reserves the right to dismiss or suspend any student for any of the following reasons:</p>
<p align="justify">1. Academic deficiencies</p>
<p align="justify">2. Failure to gain acceptance into a major field of study</p>
<p align="justify">3. Conduct deemed to be detrimental to the interests of the College</p>
<p align="justify">In such cases neither the College nor any of its officers shall be under any liability whatsoever for such dismissal or suspension. &nbsp;<strong>The College will not accept transfer courses from any institution earned while a student is serving a disciplinary suspension.</strong></p>
<p align="justify">A student who has been dismissed from the College may not enroll in the regular day session of the College or in the Wescoe School, either as a full-time or special student.</p>
<p align="justify">A student who fails to achieve good standing by the end of his or her probationary period will be dismissed from the College. &nbsp;Under rare circumstances, a student so dismissed for academic reasons may be readmitted upon formal application to the Dean of Academic Life after the lapse of at least one academic year. &nbsp;Such an application should give evidence of promise to attain a degree. &nbsp;If the application is approved, readmission will be probationary for a period of one semester only. &nbsp;<strong>A second dismissal will be final and no application for readmission will be entertained.&nbsp;</strong>&nbsp; Readmitted students must fulfill the General Academic Requirements that are in force as of the term of readmission. &nbsp;For additional information on being readmitted to Muhlenberg College, see <strong>Readmission.</strong></p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#12" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="12">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="1">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          ACADEMIC INTEGRITY CODE
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="12" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="1">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">The Academic Integrity Code is a communal expression of the importance of academic honesty and integrity. &nbsp;The Code, to which every student is required to subscribe, governs all activities involving the academic work of the student. &nbsp;The Code also governs the bases for evaluating intellectual achievement, written or oral, including examinations, quizzes, tests, themes, reports, recitations, and laboratory exercises. &nbsp;The Academic Integrity Code is printed in full in the Student Policy and Information Guide, and students and faculty should familiarize themselves with its provisions.</p>
<p><strong><span class="italic"><em>Adherence to the Policies of the Academic Integrity Code:</em> </span></strong></p>
<p align="justify">Muhlenberg College has established an Academic Integrity Code because of its belief that academic honesty is a matter of individual responsibility and that, when standards of honesty are violated, members of the community are harmed.&nbsp; As a prerequisite for matriculation each student must pledge to adhere to the provisions of this Academic Integrity Code. &nbsp;On all work submitted for a grade students shall write and sign the following pledge: "I pledge that I have complied with the Academic Integrity Code in this work." &nbsp;Some faculty will accept "AIC". &nbsp;Violations of the Academic Integrity Code include, but are not limited to, cheating during examinations, plagiarism, collusion, false information, and helping or hindering others.</p>
<p align="justify">Each faculty member shall identify the procedures to be used for classroom examinations and other assignments in each course. &nbsp;<span class="italic"><em>It is against College policy for a faculty member to accept any work submitted for a grade without the student's signed Academic Integrity Code pledge.</em> </span></p>
<p align="justify">Class tests and final examinations should be proctored. &nbsp;Proctoring is defined as having a faculty member present in the room. &nbsp;Proctoring is the responsibility of the faculty member teaching the course but, in special situations, that responsibility may be delegated to faculty colleagues.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#42" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="42">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="4">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          ACADEMIC POLICY COMMITTEE (APC) 
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="42" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="4">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>The Academic Policy Committee (APC) is responsible for the establishment and implementation of all academic requirements and regulations for degrees and for long-range planning in academic areas. &nbsp;The Committee has seven faculty members, the Provost, the Dean of Academic Life, and the Registrar ex officio, and two student members.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#52" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="52">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="5">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          ACADEMIC RECORDS
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="52" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="5">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">A permanent academic record is prepared for each student who registers at Muhlenberg College.&nbsp; An unabridged transcript of this record is maintained in the Office of the Registrar.&nbsp;</p>
<p align="justify">Upon graduation or withdrawal from the College, a student's academic record continues to be stored on a permanent basis in the Office of the Registrar with a second copy stored in another location on campus.</p>
<p align="justify">A copy of the permanent record may be released only upon the written consent of the individual student. &nbsp;Any student requesting to inspect and review educational records may do so by submitting their request to the Office of the Registrar.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#62" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="62">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="6">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          ACADEMIC RENEWAL
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="62" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="6">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Academic Renewal is extended to former Muhlenberg students who have not been enrolled at the College for at least 10 years. &nbsp;It allows them to remove from their cumulative GPA previously taken coursework. &nbsp;This option may be exercised pursuant to the following regulations:</p>
<p align="justify">1. The student must consult with the Dean of the Wescoe School, and the Dean must approve course selection before the student may enroll.</p>
<p align="justify">2. The option may be exercised only after three course units have been completed with a grade of "C" or better. &nbsp;The student must initiate the procedure; it will not be automatic.</p>
<p align="justify">3. All courses and grades will remain on the student's transcript and be used for graduation honors; previous courses with grades of D or F will not be included in the calculation of the cum GPA.</p>
<p align="justify">4. Courses in which grades of "C-" or better were earned prior to return will be counted toward degree requirements.</p>
<p align="justify">5. Courses based on credit hours will be converted to course units according to the existing course conversion procedures which apply to all Muhlenberg students.</p>
<p align="justify">6. This option can be extended only once to any individual student.</p>
    </div>
  </div>

  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion"

     aria-controls="82">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="8">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          ACCOUNTING: 150 SEMESTER HOUR PROGRAM
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="82" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="8">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">The accounting program at Muhlenberg includes several options for completing the 150 semester hours of education encouraged by the American Institute of Certified Public Accountants and required by some states prior to receiving a license to practice as a CPA. &nbsp;It is very important that students planning to exercise one of these options plan their program at Muhlenberg carefully.</p>
<p align="justify">Students may choose to receive their bachelor's degree at Muhlenberg and enroll in additional coursework at a later time, either at Muhlenberg or another institution. &nbsp;Two other options also exist. Students may take four additional course units at Muhlenberg, above and beyond bachelor degree requirements for a major in accounting. &nbsp;As another option, Muhlenberg has an articulation agreement with Lehigh University. &nbsp;Exceptional students can carefully plan their coursework at Muhlenberg and be admitted into the Lehigh Master of Science in Accounting and Information Analysis program.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#92" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="92">
  	<div class="panel-heading"

      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          ACHIEVEMENT TESTS
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>

  <div id="92" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="9">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Exemption from the foreign language requirement will be granted to students who have at least three years of language (French, German, Hebrew, Italian, Latin, Spanish, or Russian) in high school and achieved a score of 650 or above on the College Board Achievement Test.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#102" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="102">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="10">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          ADDING COURSES
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="102" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="10">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Students may add courses without faculty approval through the first five class days of the traditional semester; courses may continue to be added through the following three class days of the traditional semester with faculty approval; courses may be dropped without approval or academic penalty through the first eight class days of the traditional semester. &nbsp;Enrollment in courses is closed at the conclusion of the add/drop period. The last day to add and drop is identified each semester on the College's academic calendar.</p>
<p align="justify">A student may enroll in a course until the deadline specified on the Academic Calendar which is published on the web. &nbsp;Course entry is accomplished by logging in to CapStone Online, adding the course on the registration form, and submitting the form. &nbsp;Students are informed of success or failure to add via notes written at the top of the screen. &nbsp;All adds must be accomplished before the posted deadline. &nbsp;Failure to add the course by the deadline will result in lack of registration and may result in denial of course credit.</p>
<p align="justify">First-semester students interested in registering for Ensembles or Applied Music will do so in the Music Office (CA 155). &nbsp;Starting in their second semester, students will register for Ensembles and Applied Music on Capstone. &nbsp;For voice lessons, students will need approval from their desired instructor before registering; new voice students should contact the Music Office to set up an audition and be assigned a voice teacher. Registration for instrumental lessons is unrestricted. &nbsp;Once registered, students will select a lesson time by following the "Applied Lessons" link from the Music Department web page. &nbsp;There is an additional fee for lessons.</p>
<p align="justify"><strong>All students are responsible for their own enrollment. &nbsp;Failure to properly add, drop, or withdraw from a course may result in no course units awarded and/or a failing grade. </strong></p>
    </div>
  </div>

      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          ADMINISTRATIVE DROPS
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="122" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="12">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">A student who does not attend the first meeting of a course <strong>may be</strong> dropped from the course in order to make room for students waiting to enroll. <strong><span class="italic"><em>Students should not assume, however, that missing the first course meeting ensures that they will be dropped from a course</em>. </span></strong>Non-attendance drops will be processed only at the instructor's request. &nbsp;Again, all students are responsible for their own enrollment; failure to properly add, drop, or withdraw from a course may result in the award of no course units and/or a failing grade.</p>
<p align="justify">Any instructor who wishes to drop a student following the FIRST day of class should send an email to the Office of the Registrar. Please indicate the student's name, BergID, and the course number. The Registrar's staff will send a letter to the student, advisor, and instructor informing them of the drop. &nbsp;Should the student wish to get back into the course, s/he must add the course by using CapStone Online. Any problems (i.e. course is closed) must be addressed with the instructor of the course.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#132" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="132">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="13">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          ADVANCED PLACEMENT
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="132" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="13">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Students who obtain an Advanced Placement (AP) score of 4 (well qualified) or 5 (extremely well qualified) will be offered a course unit credit in the appropriate discipline that will apply toward one of the 34 course units required for graduation and satisfy the corresponding general academic requirement at Muhlenberg. Some departments apply AP credits toward their major requirements; some do not. Students who later choose to or are required to register for the equivalent course will forfeit the AP credit. &nbsp;</p>
<p align="justify">At least 17 course units must be completed at Muhlenberg College. Consequently, no more than 17 non-Muhlenberg course units (whether transferred or awarded for test scores) may contribute to the 34 course units required to earn a bachelorâ€™s degree at Muhlenberg.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
<p align="justify">Students who did not indicate Muhlenberg College as a recipient of their test scores at the time they took the test should contact AP services ( P.O. Box 6671 Princeton NJ 08541-6671 Telephone: 609-921-9000) to have the scores sent to the Office of the Registrar at Muhlenberg College. (Muhlenberg's College Code is 2424.)</p>
<p align="justify">The Advanced Placement Program at Muhlenberg is coordinated by the Office of the Registrar in conjunction with the various academic departments. Any procedural questions should be directed to the Office of the Registrar. Questions regarding specific action taken on test results should be addressed to the appropriate department chair.</p>
<p align="justify">Students who have taken Advanced Placement Examinations will be informed in August prior to the start of the semester of placement and/or credit awarded. The student should inform his or her summer advisor of tests completed.</p>

</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#142" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="142">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="14">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          ADVISING
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="142" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="14">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Faculty advisors and student advisees are engaged in an <span class="underline">Advising Partnership</span> with mutual expectations and responsibilities. &nbsp;The faculty advisor serves as a knowledgeable mentor who will suggest, encourage, interpret, and guide. &nbsp;The advisor helps the student with choices about programs, courses, instructors, class schedules, and general education requirements. &nbsp;The advisee is an engaged, informed partner in regular contact with the advisor and ready to discuss his/her own research into academic choices at the College. &nbsp;Ultimately, the student is responsible for her/his academic career. &nbsp;The student, not the parent, is the full partner with the advisor.</p>
<p align="justify">The&nbsp;Dean of Academic Life assigns each first-year student a faculty advisor after June Advising, based on the student's First-Year Seminar. &nbsp;When the student declares a major field of study, the department chair or program director will assign an advisor from within the department/program. &nbsp;The student may also request a particular professor to be the faculty advisor. &nbsp;This request may be granted as long as both the requested professor and the department chair/program director agree to the arrangement. &nbsp;Department Chairs, Program Directors, and the Registrar oversee the reassignment of advisees from faculty who are on sabbatical or other leaves or have left the College.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#152" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="152">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="15">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          APPLICATION FOR DEGREE
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="152" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="15">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>In the fall semester of the senior year each student completes an Application for Degree. By signing this form the student indicates his/her intention to graduate from Muhlenberg College. This form is used to order the diploma, cap, and gown as well as to provide the College with legacy, activities, and local newspaper information.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#162" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="162">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="16">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          APPLIED MUSIC COURSES
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="162" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="16">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Study in voice, piano, organ, and the various string, brass, woodwind, and percussion instruments is available in the form of thirteen 45-minute lessons or ten 60-minute lessons with a minimum of five hours of mandatory practice time per week. &nbsp;Attendance at recitals and concerts is required. &nbsp;An additional fee is charged for this instruction and <strong>is not refundable following the official add/drop period</strong>. Applied music may not be taken pass/fail. Two half-unit individual applied music courses in one instrument or voice may be counted as one course to satisfy the Arts Division (AR) requirement.</p>
<p align="justify">First-semester students interested in registering for Applied Music will do so in the Music Office (CA 155). Starting in their second semester, students will register for Applied Music on Capstone. &nbsp;For voice lessons students will need prior approval from their desired instructor before registering; new voice students should contact the Music Office to set up an audition and be assigned a voice teacher. Registration for instrumental lessons is unrestricted. Once registered, students will select a lesson time by following the "Applied Lessons" link from the Music Department web page.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#172" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="172">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="17">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          ARMY ROTC
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="172" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="17">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Muhlenberg, in cooperation with Lehigh University, offers a voluntary Army Reserve Officer Training Corps (AROTC) Program, within the terms of the cross-registration agreement between the two schools. Grades and course work completed in the 4-year Army ROTC program will be included in the student's academic record at Muhlenberg College. However, only the final 2 courses in the program (100 level MS courses) may be counted toward the 34 course unit graduation requirement. Additional information on the program is available in the Office of the Registrar or the Department of Military Science at Lehigh University (<a href="http://www.lehigh.edu/%7Einmil/" target="_blank">www.lehigh.edu/~inmil/</a>).</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#182" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="182">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="18">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          AUDITING COURSES
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="182" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="18">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Students in good academic standing may audit one course per semester with the approval of the instructor. Instructors must explicitly detail their expectations for students auditing their courses at the beginning of the semester, and students must seek the consent of their faculty advisor. Typically, students auditing a course are expected to complete all assignments and participate in class discussions but may not be required to submit written work or take exams. Students may change a course from audit (no course unit attempted) to a regular course unit basis or vice versa during the add/drop period with the approval of the instructor and the faculty advisor by completing an Audit Request form and submitting it to the Office of the Registrar. The student's transcript will list the audited course with a grade of "AU" if the student has satisfactorily completed the audit. If the student fails to fulfill the expectations of the audit, no notation will appear on the transcript. Because an audit carries no course credit, a student may register for up to 5.5 course units and audit a class in the same semester.</p>
    </div>
  </div>

  <h3><strong><a id="b"></a>B <a href="#up">&zwnj;</a></strong></h3></div>

</div>
</div>
<div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#192" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="192">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="19">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          BASIC DATA - Essential Data correction
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="192" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="19">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Students must notify the Office of the Registrar if there is a change in home address/telephone, off-campus address/telephone, an incorrect social security number, and/or if an additional parent address is needed. Forms are available in the Office of the Registrar.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#202" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="202">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="20">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          BERG ID - Student Identification Number
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="202" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="20">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>The primary means of identification at Muhlenberg College is a randomly generated student identification number - a BergID. This nine-digit number, in the format "00-9999999", will always begin with "00" and will be used by Muhlenberg to keep track of educational records. It will be required as identification on forms, to enter the CapStone Online Student Information System, and to transact other business at the College. While disclosure of this number to authorized college personnel is necessary, the number is still a personal identifier and should be guarded against dissemination.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><!-- WYSIWYG - wrap all WYSIWYG text areas in `.typography` -->
<div class="typography">
<div class="fs-row">
<div class="fs-cell fs-lg-8">


  <h3><strong><a id="c"></a>C</strong></h3></div>

</div>
</div>
<div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#212" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="212">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="21">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          CAPSTONE ONLINE
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="212" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="21">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Capstone Online permits Muhlenberg College faculty, staff, and students immediate access to the most accurate and up-to-date student enrollment records. To enter Capstone Online, individuals must access a secure server. The server helps to protect the privacy of information shared via Capstone Online. It uses digital certificates to verify the source of Capstone Online data as genuine and a secure socket layer to encrypt data transfers, making it very difficult for unauthorized parties to intercept or copy information.</p>
<p align="justify"><strong>Training for Faculty and Staff: </strong>all new faculty and staff should attend one of the training sessions offered by the Office of the Registrar on how to use Capstone Online to access class lists, obtain information on advisees and students in course(s), and enter mid-semester and final grades. After the training a profile will be created and a password assigned.</p>
<p align="justify"><strong>Training for Students: </strong>all first year students receive a password in the mail to their home address in July. Also included in the letter are basic instructions to help students access Capstone Online. Additional information and assistance may be obtained in the Office of the Registrar.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#222" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="222">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="22">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          CLASS ATTENDANCE
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="222" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="22">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Students are expected to attend classes regularly and are responsible for governing themselves in this matter. Interaction in the classroom enhances learning and is usually a significant part of how students' overall performance will be evaluated.</p>
<p align="justify">While the College recognizes the value of extracurricular experience, the academic program has priority at Muhlenberg. &nbsp;Moreover, scheduled classes have priority over all other activities. In cases of unavoidable conflicts, students have the responsibility of informing their instructors as soon as possible and reaching some kind of acceptable resolution. &nbsp;Absence from a class will not be accepted as an excuse for not mastering class material. The student is responsible for all information presented and for the discussion and conceptual analysis that take place during classes. &nbsp;(See also Religious Holidays and Class Attendance)</p>
<p align="justify">Instructors should inform students in the first week of class of their policy regarding the relationship between attendance, interaction in the classroom, and evaluation in the course.</p>
<p align="justify">A student who does not attend the first meeting of a course <strong>may be</strong> dropped from the course in order to make room for students waiting to enroll. <em><strong><span class="italic">Students should not assume, however, that </span></strong></em><span class="italic"> <strong><em>missing the first course meeting ensures that they will be dropped from a course</em>.</strong>&nbsp;&nbsp;</span>Non-attendance drops will be processed only at the instructor's request. &nbsp;All students are responsible for their own enrollment; failure to properly add, drop, or withdraw from a course may result in the award of no course units and/or a failing grade.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#232" 
     aria-expanded="false"

          CLASS STANDING
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="232" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="23">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p><strong>Class Standing:</strong> &nbsp;based on a student's cumulative graduation units<br /><br /></p>

    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#242" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="242">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="24">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          CLASS YEAR
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="242" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="24">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>While a student's application term and first term of enrollment will not change, his/her class year and expected date of graduation may change. Reclassification may occur routinely or be initiated at a student's request. Students having enough graduation units may request to graduate earlier than their current expected date of graduation. Conversely, students who do not have enough units to graduate will be notified by the Office of the Registrar of their revised expected date of graduation. Typically, the expected date of graduation and class year will be in agreement with one another. &nbsp;Class year may be changed at any time. If a student leaves the college without graduating, the expected date of graduation will be deleted, but all other classifications will remain.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#252" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="252">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="25">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          CLOSED COURSES (Fully Enrolled)
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="252" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="25">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Department Chairs and Program Directors set the course enrollment limits when planning the Master Course Schedule. If a course closes during registration, the student must see the Department Chair or Program Director who controls the seat limits during the registration period. &nbsp;The Office of the Registrar does not keep waiting lists. During the add/drop period the instructor may allow a student into a closed course by entering a Course Permission in Capstone Online. The student will then need to register for the course.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#262" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="262">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="26">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          CLUSTER REQUIREMENT
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="262" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="26">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">The Cluster requirement is one of the elements in the general education program and must be completed by all students matriculating Fall 2013 through Spring 2017, typically in their sophomore year. (Students matriculating Fall 2017 and after should see the <strong>Integrative Learning Requirement</strong>.)&nbsp;Successfully completing the cluster will demonstrate that students have achieved Muhlenberg's learning goal of building a broad disciplinary and interdisciplinary knowledge base.</p>
<p align="justify">1. Cluster courses support the development of integrative learning.</p>
<ul style="list-style-type: circle;">
<li>
<p>The challenges facing us are increasingly complex and will become more so in our information-rich environment. To navigate these complexities and work toward just solutions, students need the ability to integrate knowledge from more than one perspective or discipline in order to understand and solve real-world problems.&nbsp;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Cluster courses include integrated learning assignments - assignments incorporating two or more disciplines as a way to develop complex and interdisciplinary thinking.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>2. Interdisciplinary thinking and learning is a necessary skill for today's graduates as they pursue careers in multiple fields.</p>
<ul style="list-style-type: circle;">
<li>
<p>Increasingly, employers cite the ability to think creatively across different disciplines as essential to success in the modern job market.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Clustering provides opportunities for students to learn and use concepts, research methods, and theories of two related academic disciplines to inquire into common questions, problems, and themes posed by faculty with complementary expertise.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#272" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="272">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="27">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          COLLEGE LEVEL EVALUATION PROGRAM: WESCOE SCHOOL
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="272" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="27">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Muhlenberg College recognizes that returning adults may have acquired college-level knowledge outside of the classroom through formal or informal study as well as life and work experience. &nbsp;To evaluate this learning the Wescoe School uses the standards developed by the American Council of Education, regarding acceptance of College Level Examination Program (CLEP) scores, Program for Non-collegiate Sponsored Instruction (PONSI) recommendations, and portfolio assessment.</p>
<p align="justify"><strong><span class="italic">CLEP: </span></strong> Muhlenberg Wescoe School students who register for CLEP examinations should have official score reports sent to the Dean of the Wescoe School. &nbsp;Students wishing to submit scores from prior CLEP examinations will need official transcripts from the Education Testing Service. &nbsp;Scores that meet the American Council of Education minimums (those equivalent to a C-) will be accepted as transfer courses.</p>
<p align="justify">Students can make arrangements to take a CLEP test through the Wescoe School at Muhlenberg College.</p>
<p align="justify"><strong><span class="italic">PONSI: </span></strong> Muhlenberg Wescoe School will award transfer units for non-collegiate sponsored instruction that has been evaluated by the American Council of Education and documented by the organization where the coursework took place.</p>
<p align="justify"><strong><span class="italic">Portfolio Assessment: </span></strong> Portfolios of work or life experience that have been assessed and granted credit through Thomas Edison College of New Jersey will be accepted as transfer units to Muhlenberg College.</p>
<p align="justify">Acceptance of any credit for prior learning in lieu of courses in the major will be at the discretion of the department chair. &nbsp;All credit for prior learning will be considered transfer credit and is subject to the same conditions as traditional college transfer credit.</p>
<p align="justify">The Dean of the Wescoe School will forward to the Office of the Registrar original score reports or official ETS transcripts along with an Advanced Standing Form that provides the equivalent course and grade. &nbsp;For PONSI or Portfolio Assessment, credit appropriate documentation will be forwarded to the Office of the Registrar along with the Advanced Standing Form.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#282" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="282">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="28">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          COOPERATIVE PROGRAMS
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="282" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="28">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p><strong><span class="underline">Dentistry</span></strong></p>
<p align="justify">Muhlenberg College has a cooperative program in dentistry with the University of Pennsylvania School of Dental Medicine. &nbsp;Muhlenberg students who are accepted into this program attend Muhlenberg for three years and the School of Dental Medicine for four years. By completing the program, they earn a B.S. degree from Muhlenberg with a biology major after completing year one of dental school and a D.D.S. degree from the University of Pennsylvania. &nbsp;Additional information may be obtained from the Health Professions Advisor.</p>
<p><strong><span class="underline">Engineering</span></strong></p>
<p align="justify">Muhlenberg offers a cooperative 3-2 year combined plan program in Engineering with Columbia University and Washington University. While at Muhlenberg, the student completes the basic preparatory courses for engineering, including mathematics through differential equations, computer science, physics, chemistry, and advanced courses selected on the basis of the field of engineering interest as well as all other general academic requirements. Admission to the affiliated program is automatic upon recommendation by Muhlenberg for students with a cumulative GPA of at least 3.00. This program involves three years at Muhlenberg and two years in the professional engineering school leading to the completion of a B.S. degree from Muhlenberg and a B.S. in engineering from the cooperative institution. The 4-2 program involves completion of a B.S. degree in four years at Muhlenberg, then continuing in the engineering program for 1&frac12; to 2 years, leading to a B.S. degree in engineering. Students interested in these programs should consult the Department of Physics.</p>
<p><strong><span class="underline">Environmental Science or Forestry </span></strong></p>
<p align="justify">Students interested in environmental science or forestry may enter the 3-2 year or 4-2 year combined degree program between Muhlenberg College and the School of the Environment at Duke University. Duke University requires at least one introductory course in calculus, statistics, microeconomics, and computer science. Quantitative and analytical abilities are an essential part of this program, so math and statistics courses, beyond the minimum prerequisites, are strongly recommended. &nbsp;Before attending Duke, students must complete all Muhlenberg College graduation requirements and the requirements of their chosen major, usually biology, chemistry, environmental science, mathematics, economics, or computer science. For the 3-2 year program a student will receive a B.S. from Muhlenberg College after completing the first year at Duke. &nbsp;Duke University will grant a Master of Environmental Management (M.E.M.) or a Master of Forestry (M.F.) upon completion of the entire program. Areas of study include biohazard science, coastal environmental management, environmental toxicology, chemistry, risk assessment, resource ecology, resource economics and policy, water and air resources, and forest resource management. &nbsp;Students interested in this program should consult the Department of Biology.</p>
<p><strong><span class="underline">Lutheran Seminary</span></strong></p>
<p align="justify">Muhlenberg College has entered into an early assurance program with the Lutheran Theological Semiainary at Philadelphia. Students accepted by Muhlenberg will be offered guaranteed admission to LTSP following their graduation from the College, provided that they have completed appropriate prerequisites while at Muhlenberg.&nbsp; For additional information, please contact Muhlenberg's Office of Admission or the College Chaplain.</p>
<p><strong><span class="underline">Medicine: Lehigh Valley Hospital Scholars</span></strong></p>
<p align="justify">Muhlenberg College has a cooperative program with Drexel University School of Medicine and the Lehigh Valley Hospital. Students admitted as Lehigh Valley Hospital Scholars into the Integrated Muhlenberg College/Drexel Program complete all academic requirements of a Muhlenberg student as per the stipulations of the program as well as all program requirements of the Lehigh Valley Hospital and Drexel University School of Medicine. Additional information may be obtained from the Health Professions Advisor.</p>
<p><strong><span class="underline">Medicine: Temple University and St. Luke's Hospital</span></strong></p>
<p align="justify">Muhlenberg College has an Early Assurance Program with Temple University School of Medicine and St. Luke's Hospital. A maximum of four Muhlenberg pre-med students are accepted to the medical school each year after completing six semesters of academic work at Muhlenberg. Each applicant must apply to TUSM by August 1st, just prior to beginning their final year of study at Muhlenberg College. Students must fulfill all academic requirements of a Muhlenberg student in addition to meeting all program requirements of Temple University School of Medicine and St. Luke's Hospital.&nbsp; Additional information may be obtained from the Health Professions Advisor.</p>
<p><strong><span class="underline">Music Education</span></strong></p>
<p align="justify">For students wishing to obtain music certification (K-12) Muhlenberg offers a cooperative program through Moravian College's Pennsylvania Department of Education (P.D.E.) approved program. To be eligible for admission to the program, students must have completed a preliminary application to teacher certification, have a minimum cumulative GPA of 2.70, a minimum cumulative GPA in the music major of 3.00, a minimum cumulative GPA of 3.00 in all education courses at Muhlenberg, evidence of a successful field experience in EDU 104 or 105 or 106 or 107, at least 2 units completed in both mathematics and English, and at least 12 units completed in college-level courses. Interested students should consult the Department of Music.</p>
<p><strong><span class="underline">Occupational Therapy</span></strong></p>
<p align="justify">This program is a cooperative agreement between Muhlenberg College and Jefferson College of Health Professions of Thomas Jefferson University (TJU). &nbsp;Students can earn either a B.S. or an A.B. degree and an M.O.T. degree in five and a half years after graduation from high school. Students will spend the first three years at Muhlenberg College and then proceed to Jefferson College of Health Professions for the final two and a half years of graduate Occupational Therapy coursework. A B.S. in Natural Science or an A.B. in Psychology or Sociology from Muhlenberg College will be awarded after successful completion of the first year at Jefferson College of Health Professions. A Master's in Occupational Therapy degree from Thomas Jefferson University will be awarded after successful completion of the third year at Jefferson College of Health Professions. Additional information may be obtained from the Health Professions Advisor.</p>
<p><strong><span class="underline">Optometry</span></strong></p>
<p align="justify">Muhlenberg College has a joint program with the State University of New York (SUNY) State College of Optometry. This affiliation agreement allows selected students to complete an A.B. or B.S. degree from Muhlenberg and an O.D. degree from SUNY-Optometry in seven years. Students must maintain the required academic and personal interview standards set forth by the respective institutions. Additional information may be obtained from the Health Professions Advisor.</p>
<p><strong><span class="underline">Physical Therapy</span></strong></p>
<p align="justify">This program is a cooperative agreement between Muhlenberg College and Jefferson College of Health Professions of Thomas Jefferson University (TJU). Students can earn both a B.S. and a D.P.T. degree in six years after graduation from high school. &nbsp;Students will spend the first three years at Muhlenberg College and then proceed to Jefferson College of Health Professions for the final three years of graduate Physical Therapy coursework. &nbsp;A B.S. in Biology or Natural Science or an A.B. in Dance, Psychology, or Sociology from Muhlenberg College will be awarded after successful completion of the first year at Jefferson College of Health Professions. &nbsp;A D.P.T. degree from Thomas Jefferson University will be awarded after successful completion of the third year at Jefferson College of Health Professions. Additional information may be obtained from the Health Professions Advisor.</p>
<p><strong><span class="underline">AROTC </span></strong></p>
<p>See <strong>Army ROTC </strong></p>
    </div>
  </div>

  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion"

     aria-controls="292">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="29">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          COURSE LOADS
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="292" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="29">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">A full-time degree candidate typically enrolls for 4 course units per semester. &nbsp;The maximum course load for students during their first semester is 4.5 course units. &nbsp;During all other fall or spring terms, the maximum course load for students is 5.5 course units. &nbsp;Summer load is 2 courses at a time for a maximum combined summer load of 4 course units.</p>
<p align="justify">While students may register for up to 5.5 units following their first semester, the limit during the class registration days is 4.5 units.&nbsp; After the official registration days are complete, students may add an additional unit if they wish.</p>
<p align="justify">In order to maintain full-time status, a student must register for at least 3 course units per semester. &nbsp;Students who wish to register for fewer than 3 course units may apply for part-time status in the Office of the Registrar. &nbsp;Part-time students will incur tuition charges at the current per course unit rate plus all fees, may live in college-owned housing only with permission from Residential Services, generally cannot participate in extracurricular activities sponsored by the College, including intercollegiate athletics, and do not qualify for assistance under the College's financial aid program.</p>

</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#302" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="302">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="30">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          COURSE REGISTRATION and ACADEMIC CALENDAR
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="302" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="30">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Meeting times for courses offered at Muhlenberg occur within the academic calendar and semester timeline set and passed by the faculty. Occasionally, faculty may wish to divide the work, meeting times, and credit between two semesters. In those cases, students will complete half the work in one semester and receive 0.5 units of credit and complete the remainder of the work in a second semester for 0.5 units. Only very rarely will a course be allowed to be registered in one semester when the work is spread over two semesters. Faculty will make this request to the Registrar, and it will only be permitted if at least half of the work is completed during the semester registered.</p>
<p>Occasionally, faculty may wish to divide the work and meeting times for a single course between a semester and a break that precedes or follows the semester. In these cases, at least 50% of the work will be completed during the semester registered. If the completion of the course occurs during the break after the semester registered, the student will receive an IP (In Progress) grade until such time as the course is finished. Instructors must complete the Request for an IP Grade prior to the beginning of the semester where the course will be registered.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#312" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="312">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="31">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          COURSE UNITS (Equivalence)
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="312" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="31">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Muhlenberg College uses a course system (units) intended to emphasize the mastery of subject matter in contrast to the credit system that measures achievement in terms of time spent in class. A course as a unit of instruction may include a combination of lecture, discussion, recitation, computer work, group projects, and laboratory work. Courses scheduled for 150 minutes of classroom instruction each week also include additional instructional activities (e.g., supplemental workshops, attendance at campus lectures and performances, service learning, field work). The course is the entire learning experience, not merely the time spent in the classroom. &nbsp;Such an approach delegates to students greater responsibility for their own education and encourages active learning.</p>
<p align="justify">Each course unit is of equal value and should be considered the equivalent of 4 semester hours for conversion purposes. A full-time degree candidate is typically enrolled for 4 course units during a semester. Prior to fall 1989, all credit was expressed in semester hours.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#322" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="322">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="32">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          CROSS-REGISTRATION
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="322" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="32">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p><strong>CROSS-REGISTRATION</strong></p>
<p class="center" style="text-align: left;"><span class="italic"><em>The Lehigh Valley Association of Independent Colleges (LVAIC)</em> </span></p>
<p align="justify">Full-time, degree-seeking students who have completed at least 4 course units in good academic standing may enroll for up to two courses per semester at any one of the LVAIC member institutions (Cedar Crest College, DeSales University, Lafayette College, Lehigh University, and Moravian College). &nbsp;The student must obtain approvals from his or her faculty advisor. &nbsp;Courses must not be offered regularly by Muhlenberg College and must be within the bounds of a regular course load.</p>
<p align="justify">In the case of LVAIC courses, unlike other course transfers, both courses and grades will be treated as Muhlenberg courses for degree requirement and grade point average purposes. &nbsp;Additional information is available online through the Office of the Registrar and the LVAIC web site.&nbsp; Forms are available in the Office of the Registrar.</p>
<p align="justify"><strong>How to Cross-Register </strong>- The student should register during the regular registration or add/drop period as scheduled at his or her home campus, following this procedure:</p>
<p>1. Students will go to the LVAIC web site to search for courses.</p>
<p>2. Students review the course offerings available for cross-registration and select a course to request.</p>
<p>3. After completing the Request for Cross-Registration form, the information is sent to the student's advisor who will approve or deny the request.</p>
<p>4. Advisor approved course requests will be sent to the student's home Registrar for any additional approvals.</p>
<p>5. If approved by the home Registrar, the information will be sent to the host Registrar for review.</p>
<p>6. Registration by the host school is dependent upon course availability and registration time lines.&nbsp; Students may not know the result of their request until the beginning of the semester.</p>
<p>7. Students will be informed of the result of their request by the host Registrar.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#332" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="332">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="33">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          CUMULATIVE INFORMATION
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="332" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="33">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Cumulative information on the Muhlenberg transcript is defined as follows:</p>
<p align="justify"><strong>Graduation Units</strong> - Student's cumulative units toward graduation. These include units earned at Muhlenberg College as well as transfer units.</p>
<p align="justify"><strong>Earned Units</strong> - The total number of units successfully completed at Muhlenberg College.</p>
<p align="justify"><strong>Attempted Units</strong> - The total number of units attempted at Muhlenberg College, either successfully or unsuccessfully (excluding passed pass/fail courses). &nbsp;"P" grades are not used in the calculation of the GPA.</p>
<p align="justify"><strong>Grade Points</strong> - The total numerical value of the attempted course units determined by the grade received.</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <span class="underline">Grade</span>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<span class="underline">Points</span>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<span class="underline">Grade</span>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<span class="underline">Points </span></p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A+, A&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 4.0&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; C+&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 2.3</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A-&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 3.7&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; C&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 2.0</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; B+&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;3.3&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; C-&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 1.7</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; B&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 3.0&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; D&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 1.0</p>
<p>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; B-&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;2.7&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; F, VF&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;0.0</p>
<p align="justify"><strong>Grade Point Average (GPA)</strong> - The sum of the numeric value of each grade for each course unit divided by the attempted units.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse"

          CURRICULUM COMMITTEE
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="342" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="34">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>The Curriculum Committee exercises jurisdiction over the curriculum, including review of the entire curriculum as well as the addition or elimination of courses. &nbsp;It receives suggestions for course changes and significant changes in the requirements or structure of any major or minor and makes appropriate recommendations for faculty action. It also serves in an advisory capacity to the President, Provost, and the Dean of Academic Life, especially on student appeals for exceptions to academic policy. &nbsp;(See <strong>Petitions to Curriculum Committee</strong>). The Committee has seven faculty members; the Provost, the Dean of Academic Life, and the Registrar ex officio; and two student members.</p>
    </div>

  <h3><strong><a id="d"></a>D</strong></h3></div>

</div>
