<div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#352" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="352">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="35">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          DANA SCHOLARS PROGRAM
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="352" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="35">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">The Dana Scholars Program of Muhlenberg College provides a four-year experience for outstanding students. As applications for admission are received by the College, exceptional applicants are identified and invited to submit a separate Dana application. Invitees typically are near the top of their high school class, score 1350 (Critical Reading and Math) or greater on the Scholastic Aptitude Test, and, equally important, exhibit distinctive creativity, versatility, and intellectual curiosity. In addition, invitees demonstrate a potential for civic engagement and leadership. &nbsp;Each Dana student receives a $4,000 annual stipend.</p>
<p align="justify">The Dana Program emphasizes creativity and independence of thought through Independent Study and Research. After completing the Dana First-Year seminar, students will complete 3 other Dana course units: 1 unit of Dana Directed Studies, 1 unit of Dana Internship, and 1 unit of the Dana Forum. All Dana students must complete the Dana Forum - a capstone experience in their Senior year.</p>
<p align="justify">Dana Program participants may major in any field of study offered at Muhlenberg. At the discretion of the major department, certain components of the program may be applied toward major requirements.</p>
<p align="justify">Dana Scholars need to maintain a GPA of at least 3.33. Students who successfully complete the Dana Scholars Program are honored by receiving the designation "Dana Scholar" on their diploma and transcript. See Dr. Mohsin Hashim for additional information.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#362" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="362">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="36">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          DEAN'S LIST
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="362" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="36">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Outstanding academic achievement will be recognized by the Deans of the College each fall and spring semester. Students enrolled for 3 or more course units, having a&nbsp;semester GPA of at least 3.50 with no grades of D, F, U, VF or VW for the semester will be eligible for Dean's List.&nbsp; Students with an incomplete, in progress, or NG grade will not be eligible for inclusion on the Dean's List until the work is completed and a final grade is recorded, unless the in progress grade is for DNA 955 Dana Forum.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#372" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="372">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="37">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          DEGREE AUDITS
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="372" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="37">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">The Degree Audit is a computer program that reviews past and current student coursework and matches the courses with the requirements of his/her degree program or anticipated program, including units needed to graduate and GPA information. It will show how the student&rsquo;s courses have been applied toward the degree and which courses the student still needs to complete. The audit is divided into sections such as Major, Minor, and General Academic Requirements and will audit major one, major two, minor one, minor two, and GARs. If the student has not yet declared a major or minor, only the GARs will be audited.</p>
<p>Audits are available for anyone who has enrolled for credit as a Muhlenberg student beginning Fall 2012 or later and has at least one graded semester record in Capstone. Students in their first semester will have an audit that shows how the courses currently "in progress" will apply toward their degree.</p>
<p>In addition to monitoring what the student has taken, the audit may also answer &ldquo;What-if&rdquo; questions. "What-if" I declare an additional major or change my major. The &ldquo;What-if&rdquo; degree audit will apply completed course work to new majors/minors and show how the requirements for graduation will change based on this new major/minor. It is helpful for students who are exploring majors/minors and for those considering a second major. "What-if" can also be used to show how specific courses may be used toward a degree.</p>
<p>Toward the end of each audit is a "Not Used" section. This list shows courses that were not used to fulfill a specific major/minor/gar requirement. &nbsp;These are used to fulfill units required toward graduation. If there is a course in the "Not Used" section that should be applied toward a specific requirement, the Registrar's Office should be notified, usually through a department variance request.</p>
<p>An audit is an up-to-the-minute outline of courses needed to meet degree, major, and minor requirements. This information should be used to discuss plans with the student&rsquo;s academic adviser. If the audit identifies unfulfilled requirements, there are often several alternatives for satisfying these requirements. The student and adviser should discuss which courses to schedule based on the student&rsquo;s abilities, interests, and plans. Advising may also be helpful in determining the best combination of courses to schedule each semester in order to meet requirements.</p>
<p>In addition to indicating how courses were used toward the student's degree, it will also list cumulative and major or minor GPAs.</p>
<p>The degree audit is not the student&rsquo;s official College academic record. &nbsp;The transcript is the official record of completed work. The degree audit is a tool to provide students with academic information related to degree progress. It displays courses required and completed in the degree program. The transcript is the official academic record and provides a chronological list of courses completed and other academic information.</p>
<p align="justify">Students should direct questions concerning a degree audit to the Office of the Registrar immediately. The student is responsible for knowing and meeting degree requirements.&nbsp;</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#392" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="392">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="39">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          DEGREE REGULATIONS
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="392" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="39">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">1. Candidates for a degree must earn no fewer than 34 course units, at least 17 of them in courses offered through Muhlenberg.</p>
<p align="justify">2. Candidates must be certified in a major field of study. Typically, at least half of the courses required for a major must be Muhlenberg courses.</p>
<p align="justify">3. Candidates must earn a cumulative grade point average of not less than 2.00, based on the total number of Muhlenberg College course units attempted.</p>
<p align="justify">4. Candidates must earn a grade point average in the major field of study of not less than 2.00, based on the total number of course units attempted in the major.</p>
<p align="justify">5. Candidates must typically complete their final two semesters "in residence." A student is considered "in residence" when enrolled for 3 or more course units at Muhlenberg during a traditional academic (fall or spring) term. This regulation does not apply to students who have been accepted to degree candidacy through the Wesoce School.</p>
<p align="justify">6. Candidates must satisfy all general academic requirements with one-unit courses, except in the case of dance techniques and applied music courses where two courses satisfy the Fine Arts requirement.</p>
<p align="justify">7. Candidates may satisfy requirements in a major or minor field of study and a general academic requirement concurrently.</p>
<p align="justify">8. Candidates must attend Commencement unless excused by the Office of the Registrar. (See Graduation-Commencement or the Office of the Registrar for the policy regarding participation in Commencement by students who have not yet completed all graduation requirements.)</p>
<p align="justify">The Bachelor of Arts (A.B.) is awarded to degree candidates completing majors in the Arts, Humanities, or Social Sciences divisions. Bachelor of Science (B.S.) degrees are awarded to candidates completing majors in the Natural Sciences and Mathematics division. In situations where a student completes a major in both the Arts/Humanities/Social Science divisions and the Natural Sciences/Mathematics division, the student must choose which degree s/he will be awarded. &nbsp;The Bachelor of Liberal Arts and Science (Dual Degree) is a single degree that is awarded to students who have completed 43 or more course units and the degree requirements for both the Bachelor of Arts degree and the Bachelor of Science degree.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#382" 
     aria-expanded="false"

      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          DEGREE VERIFICATIONS
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>

  <div id="382" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="38">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Muhlenberg College has authorized the National Student Clearinghouse to act as our agent for degree verifications. Using the DegreeVerify web site (<a href="http://www.degreeverify.org/" target="_blank">www.degreeverify.org</a>) employers and background screening firms may verify degrees, 24-hours-a-day, 7-days-a-week. An instantaneous degree verification can be obtained simply by inputting Muhlenberg College and the candidate's name, social security number, and date of birth.</p>

<p align="justify">Students should consult the college catalog in the description of majors and programs for criteria for Honors. &nbsp;Honors are noted on the permanent transcript and in the graduation program. &nbsp;They are also read with the student's name at the graduation ceremony.</p>

          DEPARTMENTAL EXEMPTION TESTS
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>

  <div id="402" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="40">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Exemption from selected introductory level courses may be achieved through successful completion of a series of departmental exemption tests which the College offers during the first week of the fall semester. In some cases these tests are open only to selected students who meet established criteria. &nbsp;Other tests are open to any student.</p>
<p align="justify"><strong>Biology (A.B.) </strong><br /> <em><span class="italic">Suggested minimum of 600 Biology Achievement test</span></em> <br />Students who intend to pursue an A.B. degree and believe that they have a superior high school background in biology may qualify for exemption from BIO 100-149: Concepts of Biology by passing a departmental test in the fall.</p>
<p align="justify"><strong>Biology (B.S.) </strong>Students who intend to pursue a B.S. degree and believe that they have a superior high school background in biology may qualify for exemption from BIO 150 Principles of Biology I: Organisms &amp; Populations and BIO 151: Principles of Biology II: Cells &amp; Organisms by passing a departmental test in the fall.</p>
<p align="justify"><strong>Foreign Language - French, German, Modern Hebrew, Italian, Latin, Russian, Spanish</strong><br /> Students who achieved a score greater than 650 on the College Board SAT II language test are exempt from the foreign language requirement.</p>
<p align="justify"><strong>Physics (A.B. or B.S.)</strong><br /> <em><span class="italic">Suggested minimum of 600 Physics Achievement Test</span></em><br /> Students who believe that they have a superior high school background in Physics may qualify for exemption from PHY 121: General Physics I and PHY 122: General Physics II (B.S. course) by passing a departmental test in the fall.</p>

          DIRECTORY INFORMATION
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">

      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>

  <div id="432" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="43">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Muhlenberg College, in compliance with the Family Educational Rights and Privacy Act of 1974, has designated the following items as <strong>Directory Information:</strong></p>
<div>
<ul>
<ul style="list-style-type: disc;">
<li>student's name</li>
<li>College mail box &amp; telephone number</li>
<li>email address</li>
<li>Permanent home address &amp; telephone number</li>
<li>class year</li>
<li>major field of study</li>
<li>student status (full-time/part-time)</li>
<li>dates of attendance</li>
<li>degree(s) and/or awards received</li>
<li>College (Day or Wescoe)</li>
<li>Participation in&nbsp; officially&nbsp; recognized&nbsp; College activities (including but not limited to intercollegiate athletics)</li>
<li>Height and weight of student athlete</li>
</ul>
</ul>

<p align="justify"><span class="underline">Muhlenberg College may disclose any of the above listed items without the student's prior written consent, unless the Office of the Registrar is notified in writing to the contrary.</span></p>

</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#442" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="442">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="44">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          DISABILITIES: Students with Disabilities or Special Needs
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="442" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="44">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Muhlenberg College is committed to ensuring that all qualified students with disabilities are provided reasonable accommodations, auxiliary aids, and services to ensure full access to programs, services, and activities. Students with disabilities who are the most successful at the post-secondary level are those who are appropriately qualified and prepared for independent academic study, have full knowledge of the impact of their disability, and who demonstrate well-developed self-advocacy skills.</p>
<p align="justify">The criteria for eligibility at postsecondary institutions are different than those used for eligibility determination in the K-12 arena. Under the ADA 1990, a disability is defined as "a physical or mental impairment that substantially limits one or more major life activities, or having a record of such an impairment, or being regarded as having such an impairment". Disability Documentation submitted to obtain accommodations, auxiliary aids, and services at the postsecondary level must identify the disability, provide evidence of the disability's impact on the major life activity, and suggest recommendations for accommodations.&nbsp;</p>
<p align="justify">At the postsecondary level it is the student's responsibility to disclose his/her disability, to request academic adjustments, and to follow established procedures for requesting those accommodations. Muhlenberg College students with disabilities who request accommodations, auxiliary aids, and services are encouraged to identify these needs to the Office of Disability Services as soon as possible after their application to the College has been accepted and their decision to attend has been confirmed. &nbsp;Submission of current, detailed documentation of the student's disability with a completed Disability Disclosure Document is required in order to process requests. &nbsp;(Preferably, before the advising period in June.)</p>
<p align="justify">The Office of Disability Services will review submitted documentation, including the completed Disability Disclosure Document, and will consult with the appropriate campus professionals for further action. The student will be invited to discuss the disclosed disability and the requested accommodations, auxiliary aids, and services with the designated campus departments that include the Academic Resource Center, Student Health Services, and Counseling Services.</p>
<p align="justify">Students with documented disabilities may receive approval for reasonable accommodations to address their particular needs. Accommodations are determined on a case-by-case basis and must be requested by the student each semester.</p>
<p align="justify">After the point of documentation and disclosure, it is the student's responsibility to begin a working relationship with his/her instructor by providing a letter of recommended accommodations from the appropriate college office. The student should then meet with each faculty member and describe how the disability will impact the course in question.</p>
<p align="justify">It is very important for students to work closely with faculty members when the disability impacts coursework. They are valuable resources and can usually help the student navigate the course requirements more efficiently.</p>
<p align="justify">For further information refer to the Students with Disabilities web page at <a href="http://www.muhlenberg.edu/main/aboutus/disabilities/"><strong>www.muhlenberg.edu/main/aboutus/disabilities</strong></a>.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#452" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="452">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="45">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          DROPPING COURSES
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="452" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="45">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">A student may drop courses during the add/drop period in any semester, without academic penalty. &nbsp;For courses withdrawn after the add/drop period and before the end of the ninth academic week of the semester a grade of "W" is assigned. &nbsp;Both faculty advisor and course instructor signatures are required to withdraw from a course.</p>
<p align="justify">No course may be withdrawn after the 45<sup>th</sup> day of a semester, except for medical reasons certified by the Executive Director of Health and Counseling Services. &nbsp;If a student stops attending a course and does not process the appropriate form, a grade of "F" will be assigned. &nbsp;</p>
<p align="justify">A student who does not attend the first meeting of a course <em><span class="italic">may </span></em> be dropped from the roster in order to make room for students waiting to register for the course. &nbsp;The professor must provide the Registrar with the names of any student dropped from his or her course as a result of this policy.</p>
<p align="justify">Non-attendance on the first day of classes does not mean that a student is automatically dropped from a course. &nbsp;Non-attendance drops will be processed only at the instructor's request.&nbsp; It is the student's responsibility to make sure his or her registration of courses is accurate.</p>
<p align="justify">All students are responsible for their own enrollment. &nbsp;Failure to properly add, drop, or withdraw from a course may result in no course units awarded and/or a failing grade.</p>
    </div>
  </div>

  <h3><strong><a id="e"></a>E</strong></h3></div>

</div>

<div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#462" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="462">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab"

          ELECTIVES

      <p class="panel-title pull-right">

       aria-labelledby="46">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Electives are courses that do not satisfy either major, minor, or General Academic requirements. &nbsp;They count toward the course units required for graduation.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>

  <a data-toggle="collapse"

     aria-controls="472">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="47">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          ENROLLMENT VERIFICATIONS 
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>

  <div id="472" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="47">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Muhlenberg College has authorized the National Student Clearinghouse to act as our agent for verifications of student enrollment. Through EnrollmentVerify, the Clearinghouse will process enrollment verifications for the following types of companies: Credit Issuers, Travel Companies, Housing Providers, Scholarship Providers, Consumer Product Companies, and Requests by Students and Parents. Please visit the Clearinghouse online at <a href="http://www.studentclearinghouse.org/" target="_blank">www.studentclearinghouse.org</a> or contact them by phone at (703) 742-4200.&nbsp;</p>
<p align="justify">Through the National Student Clearinghouse Student Self-Serve system, students may also obtain enrollment verifications themselves. More information may be found on the Registrar's web site at <a href="http://www.muhlenberg.edu/main/aboutus/registrar/">www.muhlenberg.edu/main/aboutus/registrar</a>.</p>
<p align="justify">The Office of the Registrar will continue to certify enrollment verifications to Insurance Companies who require the release of a grade point average or rank in class. These requests must be accompanied by the written signature of the student.</p>

<div class="typography">
<div class="fs-row">
<div class="fs-cell fs-lg-8">


  <h3><strong><a id="f"></a>F</strong></h3></div>

</div>
</div>
<div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#502" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="502">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="50">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          FERPA (Family Educational Rights and Privacy Act)
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="502" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="50">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Muhlenberg College strictly complies with all provisions of the Family Educational Rights and Privacy Act (FERPA), a federal statute passed into law in 1974 that provides the basis for dealing with student information at educational institutions. &nbsp;FERPA regulations ensure a standard for the access to, the use of, and the release of information from education records.</p>
<p align="justify">The Family Educational Rights and Privacy Act (FERPA) affords students certain rights with respect to their education records. &nbsp;They are: &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>The right to inspect and review their education records within forty-five (45) days of the day an appropriate College official receives a written request for access.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The right to<span class="content-add05"> request the amendment of education records that the student believes are inaccurate or misleading. &nbsp;</span>The College must provide reasonable accommodations to accomplish these tasks. &nbsp;The office that creates and maintains the record in question is responsible for determining what is reasonable.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="content-add05">The&nbsp; right&nbsp; to&nbsp; consent&nbsp; to&nbsp; disclosures&nbsp; of personally identifiable information contained in the student's education records, except to the extent that FERPA authorizes disclosure without consent.</span></p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="content-add05"></span>Legal exceptions to this specific prohibition include: information released to school officials with a legitimate educational interest, compliance with a lawfully issued subpoena, provisions for directory information, and the release of information to parents of financially dependent students.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Failure to comply strictly with FERPA regulations would damage our reputation and could ultimately jeopardize any monies we receive either directly or indirectly from the federal government, including student financial aid.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>More information about Muhlenberg's FERPA policy can be found through the Office of the Registrar (<a href="http://www.muhlenberg.edu/main/aboutus/registrar/">www.muhlenberg.edu/main/aboutus/registrar</a>). &nbsp;See also Student Information Release Policy - FERPA.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#512" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="512">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="51">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          FIFTH YEAR DEGREE CANDIDATE
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="512" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="51">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Students who have not yet graduated, are under the age of 24, and have paid for 8 full-time fall or spring semesters at Muhlenberg will be eligible for Fifth Year status under the following conditions:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><span class="content-add05">Summer terms are not included in the 8 paid semesters</span><span class="content-add05">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="content-add05">Semesters where a student withdrew from full-time and received W grades are counted in the 8 paid semesters even if a partial refund was given</span><span class="content-add05">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="content-add05">Semesters where a student studied abroad or in Washington D.C. are counted in the 8 paid semesters</span><span class="content-add05">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; </span></p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="content-add05">Semesters where a student was granted a Residential Waiver are not counted in the 8 paid semesters</span><span class="content-add05">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="content-add05">Students who have paid for 8 full-time fall or spring semesters are eligible regardless of the number of units they have left to complete</span><span class="content-add05">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span></p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span class="content-add05">Students who transfer to Muhlenberg must meet the requirement of 8 paid Muhlenberg semesters before becoming eligible for the reduced tuition</span></p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Students will be eligible for the Fifth Year status for the 9th and 10th semesters (or the fifth year) of their program.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Students do not apply for Fifth Year status. &nbsp;All students who are eligible will be classified as Fifth Year by the Registrar's Office.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Students who have not completed their degree following a 10th semester but have an acceptable gpa will be given a Residential Waiver and allowed to take any final credits needed at another institution. &nbsp;Students who do not have a cumulative and/or major gpa of at least 2.00 and so will not be able to take a Residential Waiver will become a Wescoe student and follow all Wescoe policies and guidelines.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>During the Fifth Year students: &nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
<ul>
<ul>
<li>
<p>may register as part-time and follow the regulations governing part-time attendance&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>may register as full-time and will retain the student services afforded to all day students&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>will pay a reduced per course unit rate plus all applicable fees&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>may live in residential housing if space is available&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>will remain a day student</p>
</li>
</ul>
</ul>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#522" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="522">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="52">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          FINAL EXAMINATIONS
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="522" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="52">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Except for independent study, independent research, internships, physical education, and applied music, a final evaluation is required for all courses. &nbsp;An instructor may arrange to use a final examination or some other means of evaluation. &nbsp;The final examination schedule for a term will be available on the web approximately four weeks after the start of classes. &nbsp;Faculty are not allowed to change either the date or time of a final examination. &nbsp;These requests must go through the Provost.</p>
<p>Two final examinations scheduled at the same time or three in one day constitute a conflict for the student. &nbsp;In order for a makeup examination to be given, a conflict must be filed in the Office of the Registrar by the date indicated on the semester calendar. &nbsp;</p>
<p>Means of assessing a student's efforts and progress should be assigned periodically throughout a semester by the faculty member teaching the course. &nbsp;Any test or exercise that is to count more than the value of a regular class exercise should be announced at least two weeks in advance. &nbsp;Typically, the final examination should not count for more than 50% of the course grade. &nbsp;Final examinations and other graded materials, if not returned to the student in some manner that insures receipt by the student, should be kept on file by the instructor until the end of the semester following that for which the material was submitted.</p>
<p>All faculty, staff, and students must be available until the semester concludes (the last day with College scheduled final exams) at 3:00 p.m. each semester.<strong> <br /></strong></p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#532" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="532">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="53">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          FINANCIAL OBLIGATIONS
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="532" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="53">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>The comprehensive fee, room and board, and other charges incurred by the student, regardless of nature, must be paid prior to registration. Students will be notified prior to registration by the Controller or Residential Services and may have a hold placed on their account. Transcripts can also be held for financial obligations as well as the diploma at the time of graduation.<span class="italic"><strong> <br /></strong></span></p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#542" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="542">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="54">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          FIREWORKS POLICY
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="542" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="54">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p><span style="font-weight: 400;">When presenting a fireworks display, the College will make every attempt to keep noise, parking and other neighborhood distractions to a minimum.&nbsp; The College will also make reasonable attempts to notify all neighbors in the surrounding area.&nbsp; It is understood that social life and co-curricular activities are an important part of the residential college experience.</span><br><br></p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Any fireworks displays shall be set off from the Library Lawn or another location that is deemed to have the lowest impact on the surrounding neighborhood.</span></p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">Neighbors will be notified via a mailing, an email to the neighborhood watch group and a notice will be posted on social media.</span></p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">We will collect email addresses from neighbors in the ordinance zone and notify neighbors of major events that might create neighbor concerns.&nbsp; If we collect a significant number of email addresses, the actual hard copy mailing could be discontinued at some point.</span></p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">No persons are to be in possession of fireworks unless a permit has been attained by the City of Allentown.</span></p>
</li>
<li>
<p><span style="font-weight: 400;">No fireworks shall occur without the prior authorization of the President</span>.</p>
</li>
<li><span style="font-weight: 400;">Ordinarily, fireworks displays will happen no more than once in any 12 month period.</span></li>
</ul>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#552" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="552">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="55">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          FIRST-YEAR SEMINARS
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="552" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="55">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p class="style2">First-Year Seminars are small, discussion-oriented courses that provide entering students with the opportunity to work closely with a faculty member. Required of all first-year students and typically limited to an enrollment of 15, First-Year Seminars promote intellectual discussion and critical thinking, reading, and writing skills. Offered by faculty members from departments throughout the College, the seminars share an emphasis on closer reading and thinking critically about the values and assumptions underlying various approaches to knowledge.</p>
<p class="style2">Primarily concerned with developing critical thinking, reading, and writing, First-Year Seminars are writing-intensive. Evaluation will be based on students' writing rather than on examinations. The seminars will teach participants how to formulate a thesis and how to collect, evaluate, and cite evidence that supports and qualifies this thesis. They will teach participants what an argument, analysis, or interpretation is and will give students practice in constructing and evaluating sound ones. Students will also learn how to revise their work, rethinking their ideas with the help of the instructor's comments on preliminary drafts. In sum, First-Year Seminars introduce students to the life of the mind - to what it means to think deeply and to talk and write critically about ideas; they model and encourage students to participate in thoughtful, critical, and intellectual reflection and conversation.</p>
<p class="style2">First-Year Seminars are registered during June Advising. Although choice of seminar cannot be guaranteed, it is considered in combination with the student's other courses and space available. The student is mailed instructional material on how to access the fall schedule through Capstone Online in mid-July. Review of the schedule of courses will inform the student of the seminar that is registered. The seminar group forms the student's advising group, and the instructor of the seminar is usually the student's advisor. That advisor remains the faculty advisor until the student declares his/her major.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#562" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="562">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="56">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          FOREIGN LANGUAGE PLACEMENT AND EXEMPTION
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="562" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="56">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Students who have not been granted advanced standing and who need to continue a language must take a placement examination before registering in June. The results of the examination will determine the appropriate course assignment. Students seeking exemption from the foreign language requirement must take an exemption examination during the fall semester orientation period. Students who can demonstrate a native command of a language other than English may apply to the Chair of Languages, Literatures, and Cultures for permission to use that language to satisfy the foreign language requirement. Students will demonstrate competence through testing in four areas: listening, reading, speaking, and writing. See also&nbsp;<strong>Achievement Tests.</strong></p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#572" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="572">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="57">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          FULL-TIME STATUS
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="572" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="57">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Full-time status is 3 to 5.5 course units per semester. If a student is registered for less than 3 units, s/he will need to apply to the Registrar for part-time status. The student must petition the Dean of Academic Life to register for more than 5.5 units.</p>
    </div>

<div class="typography">
<div class="fs-row">
<div class="fs-cell fs-lg-8">


  <h3><strong><a id="g"></a>G</strong></h3></div>

</div>
</div>
<div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#582" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="582">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="58">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          GENERAL ACADEMIC REQUIREMENTS
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="582" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="58">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Muhlenberg College general academic requirements are designed to furnish the student with the theoretical and practical knowledge that an educated person should possess, regardless of personal career goals. Such knowledge includes an understanding of the major fields of learning; an ability to express oneself clearly and cogently; an understanding of the values found in religious traditions and philosophical reflection; an understanding of epochs, languages, and cultures other than one's own; and above all, an ability to see issues from many sides, to question what is taken for granted, and to view particular events in relation to their larger contexts. The Muhlenberg College curriculum provides opportunities for exploring and integrating ideas while challenging students to question, discuss, and think critically about their own beliefs and values. By fostering such skills and perspectives, a Muhlenberg education seeks to provide the student with the insight and flexibility needed to meet the challenges of the future. &nbsp;</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#602" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="602">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="60">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          GENERAL ACADEMIC REQUIREMENTS - students matriculating Fall 2013 through Spring 2017
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="602" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="60">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p><strong>I. ACADEMIC SKILLS</strong><br /><br />Effective writing and reasoning are important in all academic disciplines and are hallmarks of the educated person.&nbsp; The development and utilization of these skills will be evident in courses throughout the curriculum.&nbsp; Students are also required to have some knowledge of a language other than English&mdash;a skill which helps in understanding the structure of language as well as providing access to another culture.&nbsp; Requirements have been established so that all students may have the opportunity to achieve competency in these skills early in their college experience.<br /><br /><strong>First-Year Seminars (FY) &nbsp;</strong>Small, discussion-oriented courses that focus on the development of effective thinking, writing, and speaking skills.&nbsp; In the concentration on writing, emphasis is placed on the formulation of thesis, critical use of evidence, and processes of revision.&nbsp; All students are required to complete a First-Year Seminar. <br /><br /><strong>Writing (W)</strong> Competency in writing&nbsp; clear&nbsp; and&nbsp; cogent expository prose.&nbsp; Required:&nbsp; First-Year Seminar and two additional writing intensive courses; one of these must be a course designated by the major department.<br /><br /><strong>Language (FL)</strong> The development of the basic skills of language acquisition and usage such as understanding grammatical structure, oral-aural ability, reading comprehension, and writing ability as well as an introduction to the cultural aspects of language study.&nbsp; Required:&nbsp; two courses in the same language OR proficiency adequate to prepare students for the Conversation &amp; Composition course (301, 302) in the language.&nbsp; Students are encouraged to complete the language requirement by the end of the sophomore year.&nbsp; Initial placement in language study at Muhlenberg is dependent upon experience and placement test results as recommended by the Department of Languages, Literatures, and Cultures.<br /><br /><strong>Reasoning (RG) &nbsp;</strong>The ability to understand and utilize mathematical and/or logical relationships, to analyze data, to construct and assess arguments, and to make sound judgments.&nbsp; A course used to fulfill the Reasoning requirement may not be double counted for a distribution requirement.&nbsp; Required:&nbsp; one course.&nbsp; Students are encourage to complete the reasoning requirement no later than the end of the sophomore year.<br />&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;<br /><strong>II. INTELLECTUAL BREADTH</strong><br /><br />The following requirements provide some degree of breadth in the academic experience of all students.&nbsp; Courses meeting distribution designations will introduce students to the different types of assumptions, questions, ways of understanding, and results that characterize various fields of inquiry in the liberal arts.&nbsp; Within a distribution area each course satisfying that area requirement must have a different prefix.&nbsp; A maximum of two courses required for the major may be used to satisfy a distribution requirement. <br /><br />Departments listed with a distribution area below will generally offer courses with that designation, although there may be certain instances where the department may offer a course in another distribution area.&nbsp; Interdisciplinary Programs that offer a course(s) within a distribution area are listed as well.&nbsp; Because the nature of interdisciplinary programs is to span several academic areas, an Interdisciplinary Program may be listed in more than one distribution area.<br /><br /><strong>Arts (AR)</strong> <em>one course</em>:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <br />Students develop the technical skills, problem-solving ability, judgment, and courage necessary to create new work in the visual, performing, and literary arts, together with the knowledge of the theory, history, and social context of artistic practice. &nbsp;While typically&nbsp;all general academic requirements must be met with one-unit courses, in the case of dance techniques and applied music courses two .5 unit courses may be used satisfy the Fine Arts requirement as shown below.</p>
<p>&nbsp; &nbsp; Two &frac12; unit dance technique courses enrolled in a single term OR<br />&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Two &frac12; unit Individual or Class Applied Music courses in the same instrument.</p>
<p>Departments and Programs:&nbsp; Art, Music, Theatre, Dance, and Creative Writing and Film Studies&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Humanities (HU)</strong> <em>three courses with different prefixes</em><br />Students interpret and evaluate issues of human concern, experience, and expression by means of analysis, critical reasoning, and historical reflection.&nbsp; They cultivate knowledge and understanding of human activity and world views across time, geography, and culture.</p>
<p>Departments and Programs: English; History; Languages, Literatures, and Cultures; Philosophy; Religion Studies; and American Studies; Film Studies; and Jewish Studies&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Natural&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Sciences&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; and&nbsp;&nbsp; Mathematics&nbsp; (SC)&nbsp;</strong>&nbsp; <em>two courses with different prefixes</em>:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <br />Students explore biological, computational, mathematical, and physical theories and paradigms. They use quantitative and scientific problem solving skills to investigate natural phenomena.</p>
<p>Departments and Programs:&nbsp; Biology, Chemistry, Mathematics and Computer Science, Physics, and Environmental Science, Neuroscience, and Sustainability Studies<br /><br /><strong>Social&nbsp;&nbsp; Sciences&nbsp;&nbsp; (SL)&nbsp;&nbsp;</strong> <em>two&nbsp; courses&nbsp; with&nbsp; different prefixes</em>:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; <br />Students investigate how modern institutional structures and social, political, economic and cultural practices shape and are shaped by individual choices, group behavior, and public policies. Students develop an understanding of the operations of power and ideology across social contexts, relationships, and practices.</p>
<p>Departments and Programs:&nbsp; Accounting, Business, Economics, and Finance; Education; Media and Communication; Political Science; Psychology; Sociology and Anthropology; and International Studies<br />&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;<br /><strong>III. EXPLORATION AND INTEGRATION</strong><br /><br />Muhlenberg College is committed to the interdisciplinary exploration and integration of ideas throughout the four years of undergraduate education. &nbsp;We strive to enable our students to make connections between various areas of knowledge and approaches to inquiry, to prepare for life as global citizens, and to integrate what they are learning in their major with their broad educational experience at Muhlenberg.<br /><br /><strong>Cluster Courses (CL)</strong>&nbsp;<em>two directly linked courses with different prefixes</em>:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br /> Students must enroll in two courses with different prefixes that form an integrated cluster. The courses will focus on a shared area of interest, theme, or question, examining it from the perspective of each discipline. Clustered courses may double count for distribution and HDGE requirements (see below).<br /><br /><strong>Human Difference and Global Engagement (DE)</strong> <em>two courses</em>:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br /> Students must take two designated courses in the areas of Human Difference and Global Engagement. HDGE courses across the curriculum aim to broaden and deepen students&rsquo; understanding of human difference and to develop the intellectual and civic skills students require for participation in an increasingly diverse and interconnected world. HDGE courses may double count for distribution and cluster requirements.<br /><br /><strong>Culminating Undergraduate Experience (CUE)</strong>&nbsp; <em>one credit-bearing course or an assignment embedded within a credit-bearing course</em>: <br /> Culminating Undergraduate Experiences (CUEs) are the capstone experience in a major and provide the opportunity for students to clarify their relationship to a discipline, demonstrate their mastery of content, reflect on accumulated content and experiences, and open new paths for the future. They are required for all majors offered by departments and programs at Muhlenberg College and are the purview of the departments and programs.<br /><br /><strong>IV. PHYSICAL EDUCATION</strong><br /><br />Courses in physical education are designed to promote an understanding of the elements of physical well being. All students are required to successfully complete Principles of Fitness &amp; Wellness which is a semester long course exploring the dimensions of wellness and the health-related components of fitness.&nbsp; Students are strongly encouraged to complete the physical education requirement no later than the end of the sophomore year.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">

          GENERAL ACADEMIC REQUIREMENTS - students matriculating Fall 2017 and after
  </p>

            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>

    <div class="panel-body">
        <p><strong>I. ACADEMIC SKILLS</strong><br /><br />Effective writing and reasoning are important in all academic disciplines and are hallmarks of the educated person.&nbsp; The development and utilization of these skills will be evident in courses throughout the curriculum.&nbsp; Students are also required to have some knowledge of a language other than English&mdash;a skill which helps in understanding the structure of language as well as providing access to another culture.&nbsp; Requirements have been established so that all students may have the opportunity to achieve competency in these skills early in their college experience.<br /><br /><span><strong>First-Year Seminars (FY)</strong> </span>Small, discussion-oriented courses that focus on the development of effective thinking, writing, and speaking skills.&nbsp; In the concentration on writing, emphasis is placed on the formulation of thesis, critical use of evidence, and processes of revision.&nbsp; All students are required to complete a First-Year Seminar.&nbsp;<br /><br /><strong>Writing (W)</strong>&nbsp;Competency in writing&nbsp; clear&nbsp; and&nbsp; cogent expository prose.&nbsp; Required:&nbsp; First-Year Seminar and two additional writing intensive courses; one of these must be a course designated by the major department.<br /><br /><strong>Language (FL)</strong>&nbsp;The development of the basic skills of language acquisition and usage such as understanding grammatical structure, oral-aural ability, reading comprehension, and writing ability as well as an introduction to the cultural aspects of language study.&nbsp; Required:&nbsp; two courses in the same language OR proficiency adequate to prepare students for the Conversation &amp; Composition course (301, 302) in the language.&nbsp; Students are encouraged to complete the language requirement by the end of the sophomore year.&nbsp; Initial placement in language study at Muhlenberg is dependent upon experience and placement test results as recommended by the Department of Languages, Literatures, and Cultures.<br /><br /><span><strong>Reasoning (RG)</strong>&nbsp;</span>The ability to understand and utilize mathematical and/or logical relationships, to analyze data, to construct and assess arguments, and to make sound judgments.&nbsp; A course used to fulfill the Reasoning requirement may not be double counted for a distribution requirement.&nbsp; Required:&nbsp; one course.&nbsp; Students are encourage to complete the reasoning requirement no later than the end of the sophomore year.<br />&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;<br /><strong>II. INTELLECTUAL BREADTH</strong><br /><br />The following requirements provide some degree of breadth in the academic experience of all students.&nbsp; Courses meeting distribution designations will introduce students to the different types of assumptions, questions, ways of understanding, and results that characterize various fields of inquiry in the liberal arts.&nbsp; Within a distribution area each course satisfying that area requirement must have a different prefix.&nbsp; A maximum of two courses required for the major may be used to satisfy a distribution requirement.&nbsp;<br /><br />Departments listed with a distribution area below will generally offer courses with that designation, although there may be certain instances where the department may offer a course in another distribution area.&nbsp; Interdisciplinary Programs that offer a course(s) within a distribution area are listed as well.&nbsp; Because the nature of interdisciplinary programs is to span several academic areas, an Interdisciplinary Program may be listed in more than one distribution area.<br /><br /><strong>Arts (AR)</strong>&nbsp;<em>one course</em>:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br />Students develop the technical skills, problem-solving ability, judgment, and courage necessary to create new work in the visual, performing, and literary arts, together with the knowledge of the theory, history, and social context of artistic practice. &nbsp;While typically&nbsp;all general academic requirements must be met with one-unit courses, in the case of dance techniques and applied music courses two .5 unit courses may be used satisfy the Fine Arts requirement as shown below.</p>
<p>&nbsp; &nbsp; Two &frac12; unit dance technique courses enrolled in a single term OR<br />&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Two &frac12; unit Individual or Class Applied Music courses in the same instrument.</p>
<p>Departments and Programs:&nbsp; Art, Music, Theatre, Dance, and Creative Writing and Film Studies&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Humanities (HU)</strong>&nbsp;<em>three courses with different prefixes</em><br />Students interpret and evaluate issues of human concern, experience, and expression by means of analysis, critical reasoning, and historical reflection.&nbsp; They cultivate knowledge and understanding of human activity and world views across time, geography, and culture.</p>
<p>Departments and Programs: English; History; Languages, Literatures, and Cultures; Philosophy; Religion Studies; and American Studies; Film Studies; and Jewish Studies&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</p>
<p><span><strong>Natural Sciences and Mathematics (SC)</strong>&nbsp;</span><em>two courses with different prefixes</em>:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br />Students explore biological, computational, mathematical, and physical theories and paradigms. They use quantitative and scientific problem solving skills to investigate natural phenomena.</p>
<p>Departments and Programs:&nbsp; Biology, Chemistry, Mathematics and Computer Science, Physics, and Environmental Science, Neuroscience, and Sustainability Studies<br /><br /><span><strong>Social Sciences (SL)</strong>&nbsp;</span><em>two&nbsp; courses&nbsp; with&nbsp; different prefixes</em>:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br />Students investigate how modern institutional structures and social, political, economic and cultural practices shape and are shaped by individual choices, group behavior, and public policies. Students develop an understanding of the operations of power and ideology across social contexts, relationships, and practices.</p>
<p>Departments and Programs:&nbsp; Accounting, Business, Economics, and Finance; Education; Media and Communication; Political Science; Psychology; Sociology and Anthropology; and International Studies<br />&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;<br /><strong>III. EXPLORATION AND INTEGRATION</strong><br /><br />Muhlenberg College is committed to the interdisciplinary exploration and integration of ideas throughout the four years of undergraduate education. &nbsp;We strive to enable our students to make connections between various areas of knowledge and approaches to inquiry, to prepare for life as global citizens, and to integrate what they are learning in their major with their broad educational experience at Muhlenberg.<br /><br /><strong>Integrative Learning (IL):</strong> &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;<br />Students must enroll in one designated Integrative Learning experience. &nbsp;These experiences emphasize making connections that combine disparate disciplinary, methodological, ideological, or epistemological perspectives; entail applying multiple ways of knowing to concepts and experiences; and empower students to recognize and solve problems, address existing questions, and ask new ones in more comprehensive ways. &nbsp;The Integrative Learning curricular requirement provides opportunities for intentionally cultivating this way of thinking in collaborative environments and communities.<br /><br /><strong>Human Difference and Global Engagement (DE)</strong>&nbsp;<em>two courses</em>:&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<br />Students must take two designated courses in the areas of Human Difference and Global Engagement. HDGE courses across the curriculum aim to broaden and deepen students&rsquo; understanding of human difference and to develop the intellectual and civic skills students require for participation in an increasingly diverse and interconnected world. HDGE courses may double count for distribution and cluster requirements.<br /><br /><strong>Culminating Undergraduate Experience (CUE)</strong>&nbsp;<em>one credit-bearing course or an assignment embedded within a credit-bearing course</em>:&nbsp;<br />Culminating Undergraduate Experiences (CUEs) are the capstone experience in a major and provide the opportunity for students to clarify their relationship to a discipline, demonstrate their mastery of content, reflect on accumulated content and experiences, and open new paths for the future. They are required for all majors offered by departments and programs at Muhlenberg College and are the purview of the departments and programs.<br /><br /><strong>IV. PHYSICAL EDUCATION</strong><br /><br />Courses in physical education are designed to promote an understanding of the elements of physical well being. All students are required to successfully complete Principles of Fitness &amp; Wellness which is a semester long course exploring the dimensions of wellness and the health-related components of fitness.&nbsp; Students are strongly encouraged to complete the physical education requirement no later than the end of the sophomore year.</p>

       id="63">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          GRADE AND MARKING SYSTEM
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>

  </a>
  <div id="632" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="63">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Quality points assigned to each traditional letter grade, effective Fall 1992:<br /><br />&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Grade&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Quality Points&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Grade&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Quality Points<br /><br />&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A+, A&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 4.0&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; C+&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 2.3<br /><br />&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; A-&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 3.7&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; C&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 2.0<br /><br />&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; B+&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 3.3&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; C-&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 1.7<br /><br />&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; B&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 3.0&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; D&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 1.0<br /><br />&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; B-&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 2.7&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; F&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; 0.0<br /><br />AU Successful completion of audit (no course unit awarded, no GPA calculation).<br /><br />I&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Incomplete. &nbsp;An incomplete may be assigned when the student presents a compelling reason for the inability to complete course requirements by the end of the term. Incompletes will not be calculated in the GPA until converted into a traditional letter grade. Completion of the work must be arranged with the instructor and a Change of Grade form submitted to the Registrar's Office within 35 days after the deadline for submitting final grades for the semester. Incomplete grades not assigned a traditional letter grade within 35 days will be recorded as "F".<br /><br />IP&nbsp;&nbsp; In Progress. The course in which the student is enrolled is not yet complete.</p>
<p>NG &nbsp;No grade submitted by the instructor.</p>
<p>P &nbsp; &nbsp; Successful completion of pass/fail course. Course unit awarded, no GPA calculation. &nbsp;(Courses failed will be computed in GPA.)<br /><br />S &nbsp; &nbsp; Successful completion of zero unit course (no course unit awarded, no GPA calculation).<br /><br />U&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; Unsatisfactory performance in zero unit course (no course unit awarded, no GPA calculation).<br /><br />VF &nbsp; Forced withdrawal because of an Academic Integrity Code violation. No course unit awarded; treated as failing for GPA calculation.</p>
<p>VW &nbsp;Academic Integrity Code Violation withdrawal (no course unit awarded, no GPA calculation).<br /><br />W &nbsp; &nbsp;Student withdrew (no course unit awarded, no GPA calculation).<br /><br />An asterisk (*) indicates that an incomplete was initially recorded for the course; then changed to the letter grade which is currently reflected.</p>
<p>A student's grade point average (GPA) is the sum of quality points divided by the total attempted course units.</p>
    </div>
  </div>

  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#622" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="622">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="62">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          GRADE CHANGES
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="622" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="62">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Only the instructor issuing the original grade may change a grade. Once a grade has been submitted, an instructor cannot verbally communicate a grade change to the Registrar. The instructor must complete a Change of Grade form with the student's new grade, either online or via a paper change of grade form, and the reason for the grade change. After the change the student will be able to review the revised grade on Capstone Online.</p>
<p>Students are expected to request a review of academic progress during the semester in which a course runs. If the final grade is in question, a student is expected to request a review within a reasonable time period after grades have been posted, not to exceed 60 days of the end of the semester or end of an extension, if an Incomplete was granted. This will foster an environment of a timely resolution and prevent issues from arising semesters or years after a grade has been posted.</p>
<p>Once a semester has been completed and a student has been awarded a final grade (not an Incomplete or In Progress grade), the student is not allowed to turn in additional work, extra credit work, or work that was required earlier in the semester in order to raise the grade. Students may always request that a faculty member review previous work which determined the final grade, but no new work can be submitted once a final grade has been submitted. If, before final grades are posted, the faculty member and student agree that additional work can be submitted, the student should be granted an Incomplete in accordance with the Incomplete Policy.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
