  <div id="952" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="95">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Traditional day students seeking readmission to the College must submit an application to the Dean of Academic Life for review by the Readmission and Status Change Committee. &nbsp;Student applications are considered on a case-by-case basis and must present compelling evidence of success, both in terms of academic and social conduct. &nbsp;Such conduct at the College and interactions with the College after leaving officially will be taken into consideration.&nbsp; Applications are due November 15 for request to return in the spring semester and May 15 for return in the fall semester.&nbsp; Readmission is not guaranteed.</p>
<p align="justify">Students who left the College in order to perform military service will be readmitted with the same academic status they had when last in attendance at Muhlenberg. In most cases, the length of the absence from the College cannot exceed five years.&nbsp;</p>
<p align="justify">Students who have left voluntarily and in Good Standing academically should send a personal letter requesting readmission and explaining the reasons for leaving the College, activities since withdrawal or dismissal, reasons for wishing to return, and compelling evidence of readiness to be a successful student in this residential liberal arts environment. Supplementary materials such as transcripts or letters of recommendation from employers can be included.&nbsp;</p>
<p align="justify">Students who have been dismissed for academic deficiency may apply no sooner than two semesters after dismissal. In addition to the information about activities and conduct noted above, students should present evidence of good academic performance, such as a B level in at least three courses per semester or quarter at an accredited four-year institution. Course syllabi and faculty letters addressing attendance, timeliness of assignments, and other relevant factors are helpful. If the application is approved, the student will be on academic probation for one semester. Significant progress, both numerically and qualitatively, must be made toward removal from probation at the end of that semester or students will be dismissed. A second dismissal is absolute, and no application for readmission will be entertained.&nbsp;</p>
<p align="justify">Students readmitted will be provided housing following the on-campus room selection on a space available basis. Once readmitted, students will need to apply for financial aid through the Office of Financial Aid. Financial aid is not guaranteed.&nbsp;</p>
<p align="justify">Further information is available through the Dean of Academic Life.&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Instructions for Students Seeking Readmission</strong>&nbsp;</p>
<p>For readmission:</p>
<p align="justify">1. <span class="underline">Personal letter requesting readmission</span>.</p>
<ul>
<li>This letter should be addressed to the Dean of Academic Life, Muhlenberg College, 2400 Chew Street, Allentown, PA 18104.&nbsp; It must explain your activities since leaving Muhlenberg and present compelling evidence that you are ready to successfully complete your degree.</li>
<li>If you left Muhlenberg with a GPA lower than 2.00, you are expected to have completed at least 3 units of academic work with a strong GPA at another institution. &nbsp;An official transcript of that work should be sent to the Dean by the institution where you earned the credit.&nbsp; Your application will be considered by the Readmission and Status Change Committee.</li>
</ul>
<p align="justify">Only after you receive a letter from the Dean of Academic Life indicating that your readmission has been recommended, should you complete the following steps.</p>
<p align="justify">2. <span class="underline">Official transcript of academic work that the student wishes to have considered for transfer credit to Muhlenberg</span>. Please have the transcript(s) sent to the Office of the Registrar, except as in #1 above. &nbsp;(Not applicable for students on disciplinary suspension.)</p>
<p align="justify">3. <span class="underline">Completed Transfer Course Authorization Form</span>. The approval of the department chair concerned is required on this form if you wish to transfer credit to Muhlenberg for academic work taken at other institutions. &nbsp;After completing the form, it should be sent, along with a copy of the catalog description of the courses and course syllabi to the Office of the Registrar.&nbsp; Form available through Registrar's website.</p>
<p align="justify">4. <span class="underline">Application for Declaring a Major and/or Minor Program (i.e. Field of Study form)</span>. You must fill out this form, have it signed by the chair of your major department/program, and return it to the Dean of Academic Life. If you are currently undeclared, your first-year advisor should complete the form. Field of Study form available through Registrar's website.</p>
<p align="justify">5. <span class="underline">Signed Academic Integrity Code and Social Code Agreements</span>. These documents are to be signed and returned to the Dean of Academic Life. Forms will be enclosed with letter of acceptance.</p>
<p align="justify">6. <span class="underline">Housing</span>. Students readmitted will be provided housing following on-campus room selection on a space available basis. Phone:&nbsp; 484-664-3180.</p>
<p align="justify">7. <span class="underline">Financial Aid</span>. If you wish to apply for financial aid, contact the Director of Financial Aid. Phone: 484-664-3175.</p>
<p align="justify">8. <span class="underline">Controller's Office</span>. This office must also clear you before your return. Phone: 484-664-3150.</p>
<p align="justify">9. <span class="underline">Confirmation of readmission by the Dean of Academic Life</span>.</p>
<p>10. <span class="underline">Registration Materials</span>. The master course schedule for the upcoming semester is available through the Registrar's website (www.muhlenberg.edu/main/aboutus/registrar/). In order to register, the Controller must clear you, your advisor must give you online approval, and the Registrar must be notified of your readmission. You will then be given an opportunity to register for your classes for the upcoming semester using Muhlenberg's Online Registration system.</p>
<p align="justify">Readmission to Muhlenberg is contingent upon the student's presentation of evidence of promise to attain a degree and, in most cases, upon the student's acceptance as a major in an academic department. Readmitted students must fulfill the General Academic Requirements that are in force as of the term of readmission.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#962" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="962">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="96">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          REFUND POLICY
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="962" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="96">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">The College has adopted the following regulations with respect to refunds and rebates due to the withdrawal, suspension, or expulsion of a student during the semester. The College is entitled to a portion of the comprehensive fee in accordance with the following schedule: &nbsp;</p>
<p>20 percent if withdrawal occurs during first week;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp; <br />40 percent if withdrawal occurs during second week;&nbsp;<br />60 percent if withdrawal occurs during third week; &nbsp;&nbsp; <br />80 percent if withdrawal occurs during fourth week; <br />100 percent if withdrawal occurs after the fourth week.</p>
<p align="justify">Note: Student aid which must be returned to the awarding agency cannot be used to satisfy amounts owed to the College.</p>
<p align="justify">Withdrawal due to medical reasons approved by the Director of Student Health Services or Director of Counseling may entitle a student to a pro rata refund of the comprehensive fee. The amount to be refunded, if any, will be decided based upon merit. The following fees and deposits are not refundable: application fee, matriculation fee, orientation fee, reservation deposit for admission, room reservation deposit, and room fees.</p>
<p align="justify">Board Fee: In all cases of withdrawal, a refund of the contract portion of the board fee will be made in proportion to the number of unexpired full weeks remaining, provided the refund is applied for at the time of withdrawal from the College and the student meal plan is surrendered.</p>
<p align="justify">Flex Dollars: Unused flex dollars will be refunded to a withdrawn student.</p>
<p align="justify">Room Fee: A student withdrawing from the College during the semester will receive a refund of room fees only if a replacement, not already residing in the College residential system, is obtained for the room.</p>
<p align="justify">The Financial Aid Office is required by federal statute to recalculate federal financial aid eligibility for students who withdraw, drop out, are dismissed, or take a leave of absence prior to completing 60% of a payment period or term. The federal Title IV financial aid programs must be recalculated in these situations.</p>
<p align="justify">If a student leaves the institution prior to completing 60% of a payment period or term, the financial aid office recalculates eligibility for Title IV funds. Recalculation is based on the percentage of earned aid using the following Federal Return of the Title IV funds formula:</p>
<p align="justify">Percentage of payment period or term completed equals the number of days completed up to the withdrawal date divided by the total days in the payment period or term. (Any break of five days or more is not counted as part of the days in the term.) This percentage is also the percentage of earned aid.</p>
<p align="justify">Funds are returned to the appropriate federal program based on the percentage of unearned aid using the following formula:</p>
<p align="justify">Aid to be returned equals (100% of the aid that could not be disbursed minus the percentage of earned aid) multiplied by the total amount of aid that could have been disbursed during the payment period or term.</p>
<p align="justify">If a student earned less aid than was disbursed, the institution would be required to return a portion of the funds and the student would be required to return a portion of the funds. Keep in mind that when Title IV funds are returned, the student borrower may owe a debit balance to the institution.</p>
<p align="justify">Refunds are allocated in the following order:</p>
<p>&bull;&nbsp;Unsubsidized Federal Stafford Loans &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</p>
<p>&bull; Subsidized Federal Stafford Loans &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</p>
<p>&bull; Unsubsidized Direct Stafford Loans (other than PLUS loans)&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
<p>&bull; Subsidized Direct Stafford Loans&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</p>
<p>&bull; Federal Perkins Loans&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</p>
<p>&bull; Federal Parent (PLUS) Loans&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</p>
<p>&bull; Direct PLUS Loans&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</p>
<p>&bull; Federal Pell Grants for which a Return of funds is required&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
<p>&bull; Federal Supplemental Opportunity Grants for which a Return of funds is required&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
<p>&nbsp;&bull; Other assistance under the Title for which a Return of funds is required (e.g., LEAP)</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#972" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="972">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="97">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          REGISTRATION
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="972" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="97">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Course credit cannot be earned unless a student is officially registered with the College for the course. Registration for courses and sections is done by the student via CapStone Online (except for independent courses, FYS sections, and clusters). Faculty may give permission via the online system, but the student must then register for the course. &nbsp;<span class="underline">Informal arrangements, including section changes, between a student and an instructor do not constitute official registration.</span> Registration is not available to students until they have made arrangements for financial charges with the Controller's Office.</p>
<p align="justify">College-wide registrations are held twice each year: November for spring semester and April for fall semester. Specific registration dates are posted in the academic calendar and on the web.</p>
<p><strong>Registration by Alphabetical Grouping</strong></p>
<p align="justify">Students are registered by class and in assigned groups. Each class is divided into groups, with group assignments being determined by the beginning letters of the student's last name. Students may begin registering at their assigned time and continue through the conclusion of the add/drop period. Each semester the student's group will move down one or two time slots for the Class of 2017 and 2018 and up one or two time slots for the Class of 2019 and 2020. &nbsp;For example, if the student registers in group #7 the first time, the next registration s/he will go down a time slot and register in group #8, then #1, etc., OR the student may register in group #7 the first time, the next registration s/he will go up a time slot and register in group #6, then #5, etc.</p>
<p><strong>Registration of Study Abroad and Washington Semester Students</strong></p>
<p align="justify">Students who are abroad and in Washington will register using Online Registration. They will be able to begin at 8:00 a.m. ET the day their class begins registration.</p>
<p><strong>Location for Registration</strong></p>
<p align="justify">Wherever you have access to the internet - your dorm room, a computer lab, a Blackberry, etc. The Office of the Registrar on the ground floor of Haas, is available for assistance.</p>
<p><strong>Registration Planning Worksheet: </strong></p>
<p align="justify">Complete the top portion with courses/requirements completed and/or currently being taken. In the bottom section, list your course choices. Make sure you provide some alternates in case your first choices fill. Bring the form to your meeting with your academic advisor(s). S/he will review and provide information and guidance.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
<p><strong>Approval</strong></p>
<p align="justify">Only your official advisor will be able to grant you permission to register. S/he will do so online. If you have two majors, both major advisors must give you approval. Minors advisors do not give online approval. Make sure to make an appointment with your advisor prior to your registration day. If you are in the Education Certification program, you must have approval from your Education Department advisor. Also, any Education course over 101 MUST have the online approval of the Education Department. Faculty who agree to provide course permissions (i.e. entry into a full course; override of a missing prerequisite, etc.), will enter the permission online, and then you must register for the course.</p>
<p><strong>Changes in Registration - All Classes</strong></p>
<p align="justify">Students may make changes to their schedule online at any time after the initial registration up until the end of the add/drop period.</p>
<p><strong>Wescoe Course Registration</strong></p>
<p align="justify">Day students may register in courses offered through the Wescoe School 15-week session during the add/drop period on a space-available basis with permission from the appropriate department chair and the Dean of the Wescoe School. No more than one such course may be registered in any one semester and should be done only after consultation with the student's academic advisor. First-year students must obtain signed permission from the Dean of Academic Life prior to consideration of the request by the Dean of the Wescoe School.</p>
    </div>
  </div>

  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion"

  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="98">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          RELEASE OF RECORDS (including transcripts)
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="982" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="98">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Muhlenberg College complies with all federal regulations regarding the release of education records as established by the Family Educational Rights and Privacy Act (FERPA). All requests to release information from the student's academic record must include his or her legal signature. This requirement specifically prohibits telephone and e-mail requests. Faxed requests are acceptable. The student is the only person who can authorize the release of information from his/her academic record. No one else (parents, friends, spouses, employers, etc.) may do so.</p>
<p align="justify">All requests should be directed to: Muhlenberg College, Office of the Registrar, 2400 Chew Street, Allentown, PA 18104-5586. An information release request should include: student's full name at time of attendance, social security number, dates of attendance, current address, address where the information should be sent, and specific handling instructions, if applicable. A small administrative fee is assessed for most record release services. Please contact the Office of the Registrar for more information.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#992" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="992">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="99">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          RELIGIOUS HOLIDAYS AND CLASS ATTENDANCE
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="992" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="99">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <div>
<p align="justify">Muhlenberg College recognizes the importance of religious expression in the lives of many of our students. Indeed, the quality and strength of religious life is one of the distinctive characteristics of the College, attracting many students to Muhlenberg.</p>
</div>
<p align="justify">Muhlenberg College has a long standing policy that students may make arrangements to make up course work missed due to a holiday when their religion prohibits them from work. This policy means that a student will not have the absence counted against the course grade and will be allowed to complete required assignments after returning from the absence.</p>
<p align="justify">There are many religious observances (for example Ramadan in Islam and Hanukkah in Judaism) that do not require that a student miss class - since work is not prohibited. However, many of these holidays impact a student's life in important ways.</p>
<p><strong>Responsibilities of the instructor include:</strong></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Instructors will make sure that work missed for a religious holiday can be made up by the student.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Instructors will articulate clear guidelines for how a student may make up missed work.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Instructors will make students aware of the way in which an attendance policy allows for making up work missed for a religious holiday.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Instructors may give an exam on a religious holiday provided that there is an appropriate way for a student to make up the exam if it is missed due to the observance of a religious holiday. </span></p>
<p><strong>Responsibilities of the student include:</strong></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Students are required to identify to the instructor, <strong>in advance</strong>, that their absence will be for excused religious reasons.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Students must make these arrangements with their instructors in a timely fashion and in a way that allows for the instructor to plan how missed work will be made up.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Students are required to make up any work that is missed.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Students must take responsibility for honestly representing their religious commitments when missing a class.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Students must be aware of the attendance policies in their courses and should make sure that if a limited number of absences are allowed they do not needlessly use up absences that they may need for religious observances. </span></p>
<p align="justify">Campus chaplaincy staff is available at any time to help our community understand the role of religious holidays in the lives of students, faculty, and staff. They should be called with any questions; if they cannot answer a question, they will be able to refer to a reliable source of information.</p>
<p align="justify">Listed below are religious holidays that some of our community may be observing over the course of the year. <span class="underline">Only those marked with an asterisk are days on which work would be prohibited and hence would require that an observant student miss class.</span>&nbsp; Dates for the current year may be found at <a href="http://muhlenberg.edu/main/campuslife/religiouslife/holydays/">http://muhlenberg.edu/main/campuslife/religiouslife/holydays/</a>.</p>

     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1002" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1002">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="100">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          REPEATED COURSES
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1002" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="100">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Courses in which the student earns a â€œB-â€œ or greater cannot be repeated.&nbsp;&nbsp;No course shall be repeated after a subsequent course is taken (i.e. one for which the first is a prerequisite).&nbsp;When a course is repeated, only the most recent grade is included in the calculation of the cumulative grade point average and the average in the major or minor. A passing grade in a repeated course counts only once for credit toward the course units required for graduation. Both grades, however, appear on the permanent record, with a symbol next to the original grade indicating that the course was later repeated.</p>
    </div>
  </div>

  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1012" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1012">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="101">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          RETURNING AFTER A LEAVE OF ABSENCE
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1012" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="101">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Each semester in November and April registration information is mailed to all students on a leave. This packet includes information needed to register for the upcoming semester.</p>
<p>Steps to follow:</p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">You must inform the Office of the Registrar of your plans regarding the upcoming semester.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">If you are planning on returning, examine the course listings at <a href="/offices/registrar/courses/">www.muhlenberg.edu/main/aboutus/registrar/courses</a> and select a set of courses and a healthy list of alternatives.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Contact your academic advisor (email, phone) and ask for his/her input about your course choices. </span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">When your advisor is confident that you are ready for registration, s/he will enter an approval into CapStone Online.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Find your time to register on the Registrar's web site under Registration and Time Schedule. </span></p>
<p align="justify">Go onto CapStone Online and enter your course choices.</p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">You will be able to make changes through the add/drop period.</span></p>
<p align="justify">Students must notify the Office of the Registrar prior to the start of each semester following a leave to confirm their return or confirm their request of an additional semester of leave.</p>
<p align="justify">Students returning from a medical leave of absence will receive information concerning their return from the Dean of Students. See Medical Withdrawal for additional information.</p>
    </div>

</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion"

     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1022">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="102">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          RJ FELLOWS PROGRAM
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1022" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="102">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">The RJ Fellows Program was established to strengthen and develop the decision-making competencies of bright, talented, and hard-working liberal arts undergraduates. The Program's founders assert that education can be a powerful force in strengthening each individual's ability to assess the future and make wise choices, and that liberal arts education, in particular, has the potential to provide individuals with a variety of analytical, problem-solving, ethical-assessment, and decision-making skills. The Program is deliberately interdisciplinary. Courses affiliated with the program have three areas of study centering around: (1) the definition of models of change; (2) the examination, analysis and interpretation of principal moments of change within history; and (3) the development of analysis and strategies to face contemporary and future changes. The program carries a $4,000 annual stipend.</p>
<p align="justify"><span class="italic">While the course offerings vary semester by semester, all RJ Fellows must complete 4 courses with the RJ designation. In selecting RJ courses, <strong>no fewer than 3 of the academic divisions must be represented</strong>:</span></p>
<p>RJ Fellows First-Year Seminar <br />RJ Fellows Research Strategies in Groups <br />RJ Fellows Designated Courses in Arts, Humanities, Natural Sciences and Mathematics, and Social Sciences <br />RJ Fellows Symposium</p>
<p>For additional information see the Director: Dr. Richard Niesenbaum.</p>
    </div>

  <h3><strong><a id="s"></a>S</strong></h3></div>

</div>
</div>
<div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1042" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1042">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="104">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          SELF-DESIGNED MAJOR PROGRAM
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1042" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="104">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Highly motivated students may propose a self-designed major not falling within one of the departments, divisions, or area study programs listed in the College catalog. The proposal must include a coherent rationale for the structure and course content of the major and an endorsement of a faculty member willing to serve as an advisor. This proposal should be submitted in writing to the Curriculum Committee liaison after consultation with the departments involved. The proposal must be approved by Curriculum Committee and the Provost, typically prior to the beginning of the junior year and never later than the end of the fifth semester. Students &nbsp;seeking this option should work well in advance of the approval deadline. A student wishing to pursue this option should contact the Dean of Academic Life to receive the name of the Curriculum Committee liaison or chair of the committee.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1052" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1052">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="105">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          SENIOR YEAR IN RESIDENCY
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1052" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="105">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Typically, students must complete their final two terms "in residence" at the College. &nbsp;Students are considered "in residence" when enrolled full-time (3 or more course units) in courses offered through Muhlenberg. If a student intends to spend part or all of his/her final two terms studying elsewhere, s/he must get approval from the Dean of Academic Life. The student may obtain the Intent to Discontinue Enrollment form in the Office of the Registrar.</p>
<p align="justify">Official transcripts from the other institution must be received by the Monday prior to graduation when all grades are due. If not received, graduation may be delayed until October or the following year.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1062" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1062">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="106">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          SOCIAL SECURITY NUMBERS
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1062" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="106">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Muhlenberg College has formulated a Social Security Number policy that eliminates the use of SSN as the primary identifier for students, except where required by federal and state mandates, or within third-party agreements. Further, this policy restricts employee access to student SSN data except where required to conduct the business of the College.</p>
<p align="justify">Offices of the College are authorized to collect and record SSN data in a secure manner when required by federal or state governmental agencies or when required by contractual arrangement with third parties. All records and files containing SSN data should be considered confidential information and should be handled and stored accordingly. Disposal of such records must be performed accordingly.</p>
<p align="justify">All individuals enrolling at the College are asked to provide a SSN for secondary identification purposes. IRS regulations require the College to request a SSN as a Taxpayer ID for use in tax reporting (failure to do so may result in a penalty). Also, any student applying for Financial Aid must provide a SSN to the College. &nbsp;Refusal to provide a SSN may result in specific services being unavailable, including transcripts, enrollment verification, tax reporting, student employment, and financial aid.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1072" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1072">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="107">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          SPECIAL ARRANGEMENT COURSES
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1072" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="107">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Students may register a course as a "special arrangement" if a course is cancelled due to low enrollment or is required for the major for graduation but is not being offered in the current semester.&nbsp; A special arrangement is individualized instruction but the title will include the actual title of the course.&nbsp; Example: The course is listed as ENG 990-00 Special Arrangement but the second line of the course title reads, ENG 373 The Literary Marketplace. Forms are available in the Office of the Registrar.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1082" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1082">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="108">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          STUDENT IDENTITY VERIFICATION 
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1082" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="108">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p><a href="/media/contentassets/pdf/about/registrar/verifications/Verification_Student_Identity.pdf">(Click here for download pdf version)</a></p>
<p><strong>I.&nbsp; </strong><strong>SCOPE</strong></p>
<p>This policy applies to all credit-bearing distance learning courses and programs offered by Muhlenberg College, beginning with the application for admission and continuing through to a studentâ€™s graduation, transfer, or withdrawal from study.</p>
<p><strong>II. </strong><strong>POLICY STATEMENT</strong></p>
<p>All credit-bearing courses and programs offered through distance learning methods must verify that the student who registers for a distance education course or program is the same student who participates in and completes the course or program and receives academic credit. One or more of the following methods must be used:</p>
<ul>
<li>A secure login and password. Each Muhlenberg student is assigned a unique student id and password to login to a number of Muhlenbergâ€™s systems. These include the learning management system (Canvas) and student information system (Capstone). The student is instructed to keep this ID/Password personal and confidential per the Muhlenberg College Policy on Electronic Communication and Internet Access.</li>
<li>Proctored examinations; use of essays, in-person exams, and other activities that require face-to-face interaction by faculty that minimize the possibility of academic dishonesty; and/or</li>
<li>New or emerging technologies and practices that are effective in verifying student identification.</li>
</ul>
<p>All methods of verifying student identity in distance learning must protect the privacy of student information.</p>
<p>Personally identifiable information collected by the College may be used, at the discretion of the institution, as the basis for identity verification. For instance, a student requesting that their Canvas (LMS) be reset may be asked to provide two or more pieces of information for comparison with data on file, or to come to the OIT Help Desk in person with a BergID card or other verification. In the same way, a student requesting that their Capstone (SIS) password be reset may be asked to provide two or more pieces of information for comparison with data on file, or to come to the Office of the Registrar in person with a BergID card or other verification.</p>
<p><strong>III. </strong><strong>RESPONSIBILITIES</strong></p>
<p>All users of the Collegeâ€™s learning management systems are responsible for maintaining the security of usernames, passwords, and any other access credentials assigned as per the Policy on Electronic Communication and Internet Access and the Family Educational Rights and Privacy Act. Access credentials may not be shared or given to anyone other than the user to whom they were assigned to for any reason. Users are responsible for any and all uses of their account. Users are held responsible for knowledge of the information contained within the most recent College Catalog as well as the Student Policy and Resource Guide. Failure to read College guidelines, requirements, and regulations will not exempt users from responsibility.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Students are responsible for providing complete and true information about themselves in any identity verification process.</p>
<p>Faculty teaching courses through distance education methods hold primary responsibility for ensuring that their individual courses comply with the provisions of this policy. Faculty are responsible for informing the Associate Dean of Digital Learning of any new technologies being used to verify student identity, so that published information on student privacy can be maintained appropriately, and so that the College can coordinate resources and services efficiently. Because technology and personal accountability may not verify identity absolutely or ensure academic integrity completely, faculty are encouraged, when feasible and pedagogically sound, to design courses that employ assignments and evaluations unique to the course and that support academic integrity.&nbsp;</p>
<p>Department Chairs, Program Directors, and the Associate Dean of Digital Learning are responsible for ensuring that faculty are aware of this policy and comply with its provisions.&nbsp;</p>
<p>The Provost is responsible for ensuring College-wide compliance with the provisions of this policy and that Deans, Directors, and the Associate Dean are informed of any changes in a timely fashion. The Provost is responsible for publishing College-wide information on how identity verification processes protect student privacy, and is also responsible for coordinating and promoting efficient use of College resources and services, and for ensuring that College level processes also remain in compliance with this policy.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1092" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1092">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="109">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          STUDENT INFORMATION RELEASE POLICY - FERPA
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1092" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="109">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify"><strong>FERPA</strong> regulations stipulate that the College must protect all information in a student's <span class="italic">educational record </span> from being disclosed to anyone but the student without the student's written consent. These release rights begin the moment a person enrolls - the time at which a person first registers for a course - at Muhlenberg. Student information release rights are extended to all students regardless of age. (See also <strong>FERPA</strong>)</p>
<p align="justify"><strong><span class="italic"> The only lawful exceptions are </span></strong>:</p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05"><span class="italic"> School officials </span> with a <span class="italic">legitimate educational interest </span> may review a student's records if they need to consult the records to fulfill their professional responsibilities.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05"><span class="italic"> School officials </span> may release information in an effort to comply with a lawfully issued subpoena after first notifying the student.<span class="italic"> </span></span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05"><span class="italic"> Directory information </span> can be released unless the student specifically informs us in writing that it should not be released. <span class="italic">Directory information </span> at Muhlenberg includes:</span></p>
<p><span class="content-add05"><span class="italic">student's name</span></span> <br /><span class="content-add05"><span class="italic">College mail box &amp; phone number </span></span> <br /><span class="content-add05"><span class="italic">Home address &amp; phone number </span></span> <br /><span class="content-add05"><span class="italic">email address </span></span> <br /><span class="content-add05"><span class="italic">class year</span></span> <br /><span class="content-add05"><span class="italic">student status (full-time/part-time) </span></span> <br /><span class="content-add05"><span class="italic">major field of study </span></span> <br /><span class="content-add05"><span class="italic">dates of attendance </span></span> <br /><span class="content-add05"><span class="italic">degree (s) and/or awards received</span></span> <br /><span class="content-add05"><span class="italic">College (day or evening student) </span></span> <br /><span class="content-add05"><span class="italic">participation in officially recognized College activities - </span> </span><span class="content-add05"><span class="italic">including intercollegiate athletics </span></span> <br /><span class="content-add05"><span class="italic">height / weight of student athletes </span> </span></p>
<p align="justify">Students may submit a written request to the Registrar to withhold the release of directory information. The Registrar will notify college offices if such a request is made. No information can be released about students who make this type of request without their written consent. The request will be honored until removed; written notice must be received to discontinue the non-disclosure request, regardless of whether or not the person is still enrolled at the College.</p>
<p><strong><span class="italic">What about parents? </span></strong></p>
<p align="justify">Student information release rights are held by the student and no one else. Muhlenberg College can and chooses, but is in no way obligated, to share selected information about a student, beyond what is considered directory information, with his/her parents. In order to comply with FERPA regulations, however, one of the following statements must be true:</p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">we have written permission from the student, or</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">parents can provide proof that the student is financially dependent on them.</span></p>
<p align="justify">As we inform students of their information release rights, we ask them to decide whether they wish to give the college permission to share information we deem appropriate, such as course grades and financial information, with their parents. Typically, this question is decided by students during June Advising. Any information shared with one parent is disclosed to both unless the student specifically denies access to one parent. Questions or concerns about disclosure of information should be brought to the Registrar.</p>
<p><strong><span class="italic">Sharing information over the telephone? </span></strong></p>
<p align="justify">If at all possible, no information concerning the educational record of a student should be discussed over the telephone. If a personal meeting is impossible, steps must be taken to positively identify the caller before releasing personally identifiable information of any type. Whenever possible, confirm information rather than provide for its initial release.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1102" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1102">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="110">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          STUDY ABROAD PROGRAM
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1102" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="110">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">In a world that is becoming increasingly interdependent, study abroad represents a significant means by which students may better prepare themselves to face challenges of the future. Muhlenberg College encourages students in all majors to study overseas at quality institutions in Europe, Oceania, Asia, Latin America, and Africa. Our list of over 150 approved programs in 60 countries enables students to engage in the academic and social life of host institutions abroad. In addition, some programs provide opportunities for experiential learning through internships and field work research projects that integrate student involvement in local communities.</p>
<p align="justify">Muhlenberg supports two faculty-led, discipline-specific, study abroad opportunities: the program for Accounting, Business, Economics, and Finance majors at the University of Maastricht in the Netherlands during the fall semester; and the Media and Communication and Film Studies program at Dublin City University in Ireland during the spring semester.</p>
<p align="justify">Students study abroad after completing their sophomore year, for either a semester or for the academic year during their junior year. Upon receiving approval from the Dean of Academic Life, due to extraordinary circumstances, students may study abroad during the fall semester of their senior year. &nbsp;Students who study abroad during the academic year receive the same financial aid package that would be provided were they to remain on the Muhlenberg campus.</p>
<p align="justify">Opportunities for summer study are available through several Muhlenberg departments. Other summer programs must be approved by the Office of Global Education before students can apply to them.</p>
<p align="justify">Students interested in study abroad programs should consult with their faculty advisor and the Office of Global Education staff during the fall semester of their sophomore year. To apply for study abroad, students must first complete a Muhlenberg College Study Abroad application. &nbsp;Once approved to study abroad by Muhlenberg, students complete host institution application materials.&nbsp; &nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
<p align="justify"><span class="italic">Program Policies and Procedures:</span></p>
<p align="justify">1. Any student in good standing may apply for admission to an education abroad program.</p>
<p align="justify">2. All education abroad applications must be made through the Office of Global Education which is also able to provide detailed application procedures.</p>
<p align="justify">3. Students must be enrolled as full-time Muhlenberg students when participating in any affiliated or other College approved education abroad program offered during the regular academic year.</p>
<p align="justify">4. Students enrolling in any summer education abroad program for which credit transfer is desired must receive prior approval of the program from the Dean of Global Education.</p>
<p align="justify">5. Credits earned abroad in any non-approved education abroad program will not be accepted for transfer.</p>
<p align="justify">6. Application forms must be completed and returned to the Office of Global Education by the deadline date(s) specified.</p>
<p align="justify">7. Students are competitively selected based on academic performance, conformity with College standards of social behavior, and other relevant considerations. Where the program preference of the student is considered inappropriate (e.g., because of GPA requirements or academic major/minor), alternative programs will be suggested to the student by the Global Education Coordinator.</p>
<p align="justify">8. Late applications are considered on a space availability basis.</p>
<p align="justify">9. Once a commitment, as evidenced by payment of the required acceptance deposit, to participate in an education abroad program has been made, a student will not be allowed to enroll in any Muhlenberg courses or apply for Muhlenberg housing during the period for which he or she will be enrolled in the education aboard program.</p>
<p align="justify">10. For most programs students accepted by the Office of Global Education must apply for admission to the host institution. &nbsp;In such cases, the decision to admit the student is the prerogative of the host institution. Some programs do have GPA requirements of 3.3 or higher.</p>
<p align="justify">11. Program participation balance consistent with the financial requirements of the College will be maintained. At this time, approximately 60 percent of education abroad enrollments will take place during the fall semester.</p>
<p align="justify">12. Any questions should be addressed to the Office of Global Education.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1112" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1112">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="111">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          SUMMER STUDY
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1112" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="111">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Muhlenberg College offers a variety of day and evening courses during a series of summer sessions. These courses, while typically offered in an accelerated format, incorporate pedagogy appropriate for full-time undergraduate students. All course units and grades earned through summer study at Muhlenberg are attributed to the total program of the student and influence the cumulative grade point average and academic standing of the student accordingly. &nbsp;Summer load is 2 courses at a time for a maximum combined summer load of 4 course units. Summer study materials are available through the Wescoe School in early March.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1122" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1122">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="112">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          SYLLABUS ITEMS AND PROTOCOL
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1122" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="112">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <ul>
<li>
<p><strong>First-day Drop Policy:&nbsp; </strong>Please note that students not attending the first day of classes will be dropped from the course <strong>only if the faculty indicate to the Registrar that specific students are to be removed from the roster. </strong>After that time, students must complete the drop online process to drop the class.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Religious Holidays:&nbsp; </strong>The Chaplain issues a document of the significant holy days for the upcoming academic year. The holy days calendar may be found online at <a href="http://muhlenberg.edu/main/campuslife/religiouslife/holydays/">http://www.muhlenberg.edu/main/campuslife/holydays/</a>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Mid-term Grades:&nbsp; All first-year students and students on academic probation or the warning list are to receive mid-term grades. </strong>These grades are vital in helping the College monitor and assist some of our most vulnerable students.&nbsp;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Academic Struggle Notification:</strong>&nbsp; If an upperclassman is struggling academically but is currently not on Academic Probation or Warning, neither the advisor nor the Dean will have any official indication until final grades. Faculty might wish to include a statement in syllabi explaining to students that the Dean may be informed of poor performance at the mid-term point.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Thanksgiving Break:</strong>&nbsp; Thanksgiving Break begins at the conclusion of evening classes on the Tuesday prior to Thanksgiving. The College expects classes to be held as scheduled on Monday and Tuesday before Thanksgiving.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Final Exams:</strong>&nbsp; According to the faculty handbook, <strong>faculty should not schedule final exams during the last week of classes.&nbsp; </strong>Moreover, faculty and students should understand that they are expected to be <strong>available on campus </strong>until the last day of finals.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Incompletes:&nbsp; </strong>As affirmed by the Academic Policy Committee, Incompletes should be awarded <em>only</em> for compelling reasons and <em>after</em> conversation with the student. The student and faculty member should have a clear agreement <em>in writing</em> on the work to be submitted and the consequences should work not be completed on time. You should consult with the appropriate campus health professional if medical reasons are involved. For more information, consult the Incomplete Grades Policy on this web site.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Incompletes and performance/participation courses:</strong>&nbsp; There are performance/participation based courses (i.e. acting, dance, student teaching, etc.) for which an Incomplete is not feasible. Please consult the Incomplete Grades Policy on this web site for more information. Suggested language for syllabi for such courses includes:</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Since the majority of graded work in this course is based on participation and performance that cannot be completed once the course is over, grades of Incomplete will not be granted.</p>
<p><strong>OR</strong></p>
<p>Performance or participation based components of this course are not subject to Incomplete grades.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><strong>Deadline to Withdraw from a Class:&nbsp; </strong>If efforts for good academic progress have not proven successful for a student, or if the student has not attended class, that student should probably withdraw from the course. The deadline for withdrawal is noted each semester on the academic calendar. By College policy, only medical withdrawals (arranged through the Director of Counseling or the Director of Health Services) are permitted after the withdrawal deadline. Please note that students are expected to maintain <strong>at least a three-course load</strong> during the semester.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Academic Integrity Code:</strong>&nbsp; Please review the Code, which is found online at <a href="http://www.muhlenberg.edu/main/aboutus/dean-academic/integrity">www.muhlenberg.edu/main/aboutus/dean-academic/integrity</a> and in the Student Policy and Information guide. Make sure that students in your class understand the principles of academic integrity, the particulars of the Academic Integrity Code, and the potential consequences of violating the Code. Most professors include a section on the Academic Integrity Code on their syllabi and may have supplementary materials specific to their classes.&nbsp; Please be clear. Students need to know your expectations.&nbsp;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Course Goals on Syllabus:</strong> &nbsp;The Middle State Commission on Higher Education requires that accredited institutions show evidence of expectations of student learning at all levels (course, program, and institution). Course syllabi should state the primary outcomes for the course &ndash; the knowledge, skills, and attitudes that students will gain after completing the course. Course goals should align with department learning outcomes and with Muhlenberg College&rsquo;s Academic Program Goals.&nbsp; All departments should have their major learning goals posted on the department website.&nbsp;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Course Unit Instruction:</strong>&nbsp; In order to comply with the July 1, 2011 Credit Hours provision of the Higher Education Opportunity Act, all course syllabi should have a section that identifies the scheduled meeting times for the course. If the course is scheduled to meet for less than 4 hours a week (which could include lecture and lab hours), the additional &ldquo;4<sup>th</sup> hour instructional activities&rdquo; should be described. A course as a unit of instruction may include a combination of lecture, discussion, recitation, computer work, group projects, and laboratory work. Below are representative statements that can be adapted for your syllabi:</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>This class is scheduled to meet for 3 hours per week. Additional instructional activities for the course include weekly workshops organized by the Learning Assistants.</p>
<p>This course is schedule to meet for 3 hours per week. Additional instructional activities for the course include attendance at specified College lectures and events and required writing workshops distributed across the semester. These activities will add an additional 14 hours of instruction.</p>
<p>This class is scheduled to meet for 3 hours per week. Additional instructional activities for the course include 20 hours of service learning work distributed across the semester.</p>
<p>This class is scheduled to meet for 4 hours per week of classroom instruction.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><strong>Students with Disabilities or Special Needs:&nbsp; </strong>Students with documented disabilities having an impact on academic performance may request classroom or course accommodations, auxiliary aides, and services provided they do not compromise the essential elements of your course. Requests for accommodations must be made in a timely fashion, at the beginning of each semester. An Accommodation Plan is developed only <em>after</em> the student meets with appropriate, disability-related professional(s). A single Accommodation Plan indicating accommodations, auxiliary aides, and services will come from the Director of Disability Services, and will include a list of collaborating professionals who may provide additional resources and consultation about the student.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p><strong>Syllabi Statement:&nbsp; </strong>It is <em>vital</em> to include statements regarding this student population on syllabi. The following statement, whose language has met the legal test, would be appropriate.</p>
<p>Students with disabilities requesting classroom or course accommodations must complete a multi-faceted determination process through the Office of Disability Services prior to the development and implementation of accommodations, auxiliary aids, and services. Each Accommodation Plan is individually and collaboratively developed between the student and the Office of Disability Services. If you have not already done so, please contact the Office of Disability Services to have a dialogue regarding your academic needs and the recommended accommodations, auxiliary aides, and services.</p>
<p><strong>Testing Accommodations:&nbsp; </strong>Students with disabilities who qualify for testing accommodations should have a dialogue with faculty about the specifics and logistics of the testing accommodations. While tests are administered and proctored at the department level, in department space, it may be appropriate for students with disabilities that impact testing to take their tests with accommodations in the Testing Suite (located in the Office of Disability Services in Seegers Union). Limited space availability requires that testing appointments be made well in advance of the testing date. Students are responsible for setting up the appointments, completing the student section of the <strong>Proctored and Accommodated Testing Form</strong>, and bringing the form to the faculty member. The faculty member is responsible for completing the faculty section of the form and for dropping off/picking up the exam.&nbsp; Please contact the ODS (x3825) for more information.</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p><strong>Concerns about students:&nbsp; </strong>While not technically a syllabus item per se, early interventions have often assisted students with worrisome patterns. Faculty are encouraged to encouraged to notify the Dean of Academic Life and the student&rsquo;s advisor in addition to your own efforts to communicate with the student. The goal of this protocol is to help students get back on track before situations are unsalvageable.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p><strong>Student Help Desk:</strong>&nbsp; You may want to inform students of the Student Help Desk, part of the Office of Information Technology (OIT), which provides free technical support for all students who may be experiencing issues with their computers or other devices such as mobile phones. The Student Help Desk is located in Ettinger 003 and is open Monday through Friday from 8:00 a.m. to 5 p.m. and on the weekends as student worker&rsquo;s schedules permit. Email <a href="mailto:helpdesk@muhlenberg.edu">helpdesk@muhlenberg.edu</a> or call 484-664-3375.</p>
</li>
</ul>
    </div>
  </div>

  <h3><strong><a id="t"></a>T</strong></h3></div>

</div>
</div>
<div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1132" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1132">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="113">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          TRANSCRIPTS
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1132" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="113">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">A complete and unabridged transcript of the academic record is prepared for each student who enrolls at Muhlenberg College and is maintained on a permanent basis in the Office of the Registrar. In addition to courses and grades, the transcript reports academic status, grade point average, and other pertinent attendance information.</p>
<p><span class="italic">Transcripts of the academic record are available in two formats:</span></p>
<p align="justify"><strong>OFFICIAL</strong> transcripts are released only upon the written consent of the student directly to a third party, such as other higher education institutions and potential employers. If the official transcript is released to the student, it will be placed in a sealed envelope and stamped "Released to Student." If that seal is broken, the transcript is no longer considered official.</p>
<p align="justify"><strong>UNOFFICIAL</strong> transcripts may be released directly to the student upon request.</p>
<p align="justify">In compliance with federal law, Muhlenberg's student information release policy permits the release of personally identifiable information from a student's education record only with the written consent of the student. <strong>The student is the only person with release rights to his/her records.</strong></p>
<p><span class="italic"><strong>Procedure for Requesting a Transcript</strong></span></p>
<p align="justify">Muhlenberg College complies with all federal regulations regarding the release of education records as established by the Family Educational Rights and Privacy Act.</p>
<p align="justify">All requests to release information from academic records must include a student's legal signature. This requirement specifically prohibits telephone and e-mail requests. Faxed requests are acceptable. &nbsp;Students may also request their transcript online. The link may be found on the CapStone Online menu and through the Registrar's web site menu under "Transcripts".</p>
<p align="justify">The student is the only person who can authorize the release of information from his/her academic record. No one else (parents, friends, spouses, employers) may do so for them.</p>
<p align="justify">Information released directly to the student is considered unofficial unless it is received in a sealed envelope. The student should clearly indicate the need for official documents on any request that instructs that copies be sent directly to him/her.</p>
<p align="justify">Transcripts are a complete record of the academic achievement at the College.</p>
<p><strong><span class="italic"> An information release request should include:</span></strong></p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">Full name at time of attendance <br />Social security number <br />Date of first attendance <br />Current address <br />Address where the information should be sent <br />Specific handling instructions, if applicable</p>
<p><strong> <span class="italic"> All requests should be directed to:</span></strong></p>
<p style="padding-left: 30px;">Muhlenberg College <br />Office of the Registrar <br />2400 Chew Street <br />Allentown, PA 18104 <br />FAX: (484) 664-3707</p>
<p align="justify">A small administrative fee is assessed for most record release services. &nbsp;Consult the chart below for details. Fees are payable at the time of request. Unpaid balances will result in a "stop" on the release of any further information from academic records.</p>
<p><strong><strong>Academic Record Release Fees</strong></strong></p>
