    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1152" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1152">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="115">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          TRANSFER COURSE POLICY
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1152" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="115">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <div class="custom-content">
<p><span class="content-add05"><a href="http://www.muhlenberg.edu/media/contentassets/pdf/about/registrar/registrar/Transfer%20Course%20Policy%204-13.pdf">(Click here to download pdf version)</a></span>â€Œ</p>
<p>Muhlenberg College recognizes that it is a fairly common occurrence for students to supplement their academic experience here by engaging in studies away from our campus. Listed below are the policies we follow with respect to transferring credit to Muhlenberg.</p>
<ol>
<li>
<p>Almost all courses taken elsewhere must be <em>transferred</em> to Muhlenberg College.&nbsp; The only exception are courses offered through the Lehigh Valley Association of Independent Colleges (LVAIC) consortium.&nbsp;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In order to be eligible for transfer, a course must typically be offered at a regionally accredited institution.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>After matriculating at Muhlenberg, students must receive pre-approval in order for a course to be considered for transfer toward the Muhlenberg degree.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>In order to be eligible for transfer, all courses must be consistent with the ideals of Muhlenbergâ€™s liberal arts education.&nbsp; These ideals include attention to <em>how</em>students learn as well as what they learn.&nbsp; Such courses commonly include:</p>
<ul>
<li>critical thinking, analysis and synthesis,</li>
<li>interaction between the faculty member and the student,</li>
<li>interaction among students,</li>
<li>developing arguments through logic, evidence, and reason,</li>
<li>writing, and</li>
<li>faculty comments on writing assignments and/or exams.</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>
<p>Department chairs assess courses for transfer based on their hours, content, and pedagogy, using the description and syllabi to see if they are consistent with that taught at Muhlenberg or supportive of a liberal arts degree.&nbsp; Students must provide course syllabi and catalog descriptions when requesting transfer approval.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The College does not distinguish between online courses and other courses for general transfer credit counting towards the graduation requirement of 32 course units. &nbsp;For purposes of statistical reporting only, students will be asked to indicate on the Transfer Course Form whether the course is being taught online.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>No online courses taken while studying abroad are eligible for course transfer.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Courses of a vocational or technical nature are generally not acceptable for transfer.&nbsp; Remedial courses are not acceptable for transfer.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>At least 16 course units must be completed at Muhlenberg College.&nbsp; Consequently, no more than 16 non-Muhlenberg course units (whether transferred or awarded for test scores) may contribute to the 32 course units required to earn a bachelorâ€™s degree at Muhlenberg.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The college will accept no more than five (5) transfer course units during a single academic term (fall or spring), while four (4) transfer course units is the limit for any combination of summer terms in a single summer.&nbsp; No courses taken concurrently elsewhere â€“ including online courses â€“ that exceed the course load limit of 5.5 units per semester will receive credit.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Only courses for which a grade of â€œC-â€ or better was earned will be considered for transfer to Muhlenberg.&nbsp; Courses not using a traditional letter grade (A-F) will be considered for transfer only if additional documentation detailing successful completion is provided.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Grades earned in transferred courses will not be included in the Muhlenberg grade point average nor will they be used to determine graduation honors.&nbsp; In order to be eligible for graduation honors, students must complete a minimum of 16 graded (not pass/fail) courses in residence.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Accepting courses for transfer and applying them toward degree requirements are separate considerations.&nbsp; Courses may transfer as elective credits but not satisfy specific requirements.&nbsp;</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The College normally awards transfer credit to courses taken within ten years of entering Muhlenberg.&nbsp; Courses that have been taken more than ten years prior will be evaluated on a course-by-course basis for transfer approval.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>The College will evaluate military credits on a course-by-course basis for transfer approval.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>&nbsp;The College reserves the right to accept or deny the awarding of transfer credit.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Many institutions do not use a course unit system similar to Muhlenbergâ€™s. &nbsp;Use the table below to convert between credit hours and course units:</p>
<table border="0" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" align="center">
<tbody>
<tr>
<td style="border: 1px solid #000000;" colspan="2">
<p align="center">CREDIT HOUR TO COURSE UNIT CONVERSION</p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="border: 1px solid #000000;">
<p align="center"><strong>Credit Hours Elsewhere</strong></p>
</td>
<td style="border: 1px solid #000000;">
<p align="center"><strong>Muhlenberg Course Unit</strong></p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="border: 1px solid #000000;">
<p align="center">3, 4, or 5</p>
</td>
<td style="border: 1px solid #000000;">
<p align="center">1</p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="border: 1px solid #000000;">
<p align="center">2</p>
</td>
<td style="border: 1px solid #000000;">
<p align="center">Â½</p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="border: 1px solid #000000;">
<p align="center">1</p>
</td>
<td style="border: 1px solid #000000;">
<p align="center">Â¼</p>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
</li>
<li>
<p>If a student seeks to fulfill a major, minor, or general academic requirement through a transfer course, the appropriate department chairs and program directors will evaluate whether a particular course will fulfill that requirement.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Students seeking a Writing (â€œWâ€) designation for a transfer course must submit an application to the Writing Program Committee, including the syllabus and in some cases, a writing portfolio.&nbsp; The transfer course should resemble as closely as possible the structure of a â€œWâ€ course at Muhlenberg.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p>Students seeking Pennsylvania teacher certification are expected to take all required education courses at Muhlenberg.&nbsp; Exceptions may be granted only with the approval of the Education Department.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><strong>&nbsp;First-Year - Transfer Coursework:</strong></p>
<p align="justify">Students who have taken college coursework may seek credit for such work by submitting a college transcript, course description, and, in some cases, other course materials. The Office of the Registrar, working with the appropriate Department Chair, will evaluate the coursework.</p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">If a student wishes such a course to be evaluated by Muhlenberg College, the student's advisor should be informed during the summer advising period and it should be noted on the registration worksheet. At the end of June the Office of the Registrar will send a detailed letter to these students informing them of what they need to do.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">A college transcript issued by an accredited college or university and the catalog course description should be submitted to the Office of the Registrar by August 1.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Departments may, at their discretion, request additional course materials for review.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Should the course(s) be accepted for transfer, an advanced standing form will be completed detailing the course equivalent.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">All materials should be sent to the Office of the Registrar. </span></p>
</div>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1142" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1142">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="114">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          TRANSFER COURSES
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1142" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="114">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Almost all courses taken elsewhere must be <span class="italic">transferred </span> to Muhlenberg College. Courses offered through the Lehigh Valley Association of Independent Colleges (LVAIC) consortium and any course offered away from campus, but specifically identified in the College catalog, are the only exceptions.</p>
<p align="justify">Before Enrolling in a Course Elsewhere, a student should:</p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Obtain course descriptions for any course(s) of interest at another institution.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Discuss plans for completing coursework elsewhere with an academic advisor and secure his or her signature before proceeding.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Visit the academic department that would most likely offer the course if it were taken here. The department chair is responsible for the decision to approve or deny coursework for transfer as well as for approving a course as meeting a GAR designation. </span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Return the completed Transfer Course Authorization form to the Office of the Registrar.</span></p>
<p align="justify">After Completing the Course, a student should:</p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Forward an official academic transcript to Muhlenberg. Direct academic transcripts to Muhlenberg College, Office of the Registrar, 2400 Chew Street, Allentown, PA 18104. <strong>No outside coursework will be posted to a Muhlenberg record until an official academic transcript is received from the institution attended.</strong></span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">If any type of financial aid was received through Muhlenberg, a financial aid transcript must be forwarded as well. Failing to do so may jeopardize eligibility for aid in future terms. Please direct financial aid transcripts to Muhlenberg College, Office of Financial Aid, 2400 Chew Street, Allentown, PA 18104.</span></p>
<p align="justify">Additional Information to be noted:</p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">No more than 16 non-Muhlenberg course units (whether transferred or awarded for test scores) may contribute to the 32 course units required to earn a bachelor's degree at Muhlenberg. The College will accept no more than five (5) transfer course units during a traditional academic semester (fall or spring) or four (4) course units for any type of summer work. No courses taken concurrently elsewhere - including online courses - that exceed the course load limit of 5.5 units per semester will receive credit.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Only courses for which the student has earned a "C-" or better will be considered for transfer to Muhlenberg. Courses not using traditional letter grades (A-F) will be considered for transfer only if additional documentation detailing successful completion is provided. &nbsp;</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Grades earned in transferred courses will not be included in the general Muhlenberg grade point average.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Once courses have been transferred, they become part of the permanent record at Muhlenberg and cannot be removed.</span></p>
<p align="justify"><span class="content-add05">Many institutions use a credit system different from Muhlenberg's. For the purpose of all transfer transactions, the Muhlenberg course unit should be considered equivalent to 4 semester credit hours. In all cases, Muhlenberg College can accept transfer courses only with an official academic transcript from a regionally accredited higher education institution where courses have been successfully completed.</span></p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1162" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1162">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="116">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          TRANSFER STUDENTS 
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1162" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="116">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">The College accepts a limited number of transfer students for entrance in both semesters of the academic year. Transfer candidates must submit a formal application, a transcript of previous college work, a statement of honorable dismissal from their previous institution, a complete secondary school record, two teacher references, and results from all College Entrance Examination Board tests previously taken to the Office of Admissions. All appropriate forms are included with the application materials. In addition, <span class="underline">an interview is required of all transfer applicants</span> and must be completed by the appropriate application deadline.</p>
<p align="justify">A minimum of 16 courses must be successfully completed through Muhlenberg toward the 32 course units required for a degree from the College. The Office of the Registrar works with an Admissions counselor to evaluate transfer coursework.</p>
<p align="justify">Applications for transfer must be filed by the preceding June 15 for fall semester entrance and by December 10 for spring semester entrance. Decisions regarding transfer applications are usually announced during the months of June and December. If the current semester's grades are required for evaluation, the applicant will be so informed and the admission decision will be made as soon as possible after receipt of the grade report or transcript.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1172" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1172">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="117">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          TUTORING
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1172" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="117">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Peer tutoring is provided by students who have been recommended by the faculty and then selected and trained by the Academic Resource Center. Muhlenberg College's Peer Tutoring program is certified by the College Reading and Learning Association to the Master Tutor Level.&nbsp;</p>
<p align="justify">Tutoring is available in most subject areas through individual or small group sessions. Full-time day students who wish to receive tutoring should fill out an application in the Academic Resource Center before the seventh week of the semester. A student may receive tutoring from one to two hours per week, per subject area, based on academic need and tutor availability.</p>
<p align="justify">Study skills seminars are offered during the academic year. Topics generally include test taking, time management, textbook reading, note-taking, learning styles instruction, and metacognition. Individual academic assistance is provided by appointment with a Learning Specialist throughout the academic year. Students may receive assistance in determining their academic strengths and in developing their study skills and learning strategies.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><!-- WYSIWYG - wrap all WYSIWYG text areas in `.typography` -->
<div class="typography">
<div class="fs-row">
<div class="fs-cell fs-lg-8">


  <h3><strong><a id="u"></a>U</strong></h3></div>

</div>
</div>
<div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1182" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1182">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="118">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          UNOFFICIAL WITHDRAWAL FROM COLLEGE
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1182" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="118">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>If a student does not register courses for a given semester, does not process a leave of absence, or does not process an official withdrawal by the eighth day of class, s/he will be declared unofficially withdrawn from the College. The Office of the Registrar will attempt to contact students who fall within this classification and will send a final letter to the student's permanent address indicating the unofficial withdrawal following the official College census date (the 9<sup>th</sup> day of classes). The "unofficial withdrawal" will be recorded on the student's transcript. Students unofficially withdrawn will need to reapply to return to Muhlenberg. &nbsp;(See <strong>Readmission</strong>)</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><!-- WYSIWYG - wrap all WYSIWYG text areas in `.typography` -->
<div class="typography">
<div class="fs-row">
<div class="fs-cell fs-lg-8">


  <h3><strong><a id="v"></a>V</strong></h3></div>

</div>
</div>
<div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse"

    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Forms are available in the Office of the Registrar to all veterans and their dependents who are eligible for reimbursement for courses taken at Muhlenberg College.</p>
    </div>

<div class="typography">
<div class="fs-row">
<div class="fs-cell fs-lg-8">


  <h3><strong><a id="w"></a>W</strong></h3></div>

</div>
</div>
<div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1202" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1202">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="120">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          WAITING LISTS
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1202" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="120">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Some departments maintain waiting lists to enroll in a course closed at registration. Students should speak with the department chair or instructor of the course. The waiting list does not negate the College-wide deadline for adding a course or constitute a promise on the part of the College that a closed course will be open at a later date. The Registrar does not maintain waiting lists.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1212" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1212">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="121">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          WASHINGTON SEMESTER
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1212" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="121">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p>Muhlenberg cooperates with thirteen colleges in the Lutheran College Washington consortium who together offer a semester in Washington. The semester (fall or spring) is designed for juniors and seniors representing a variety of academic majors. In addition to seminars and field trips drawing upon the special resources available in Washington, there are hundreds of internship possibilities in government, social service agencies, religious groups, medicine, public interest organizations, business, and the arts. Participants also experience living and working in our capital with students from other Lutheran colleges throughout the United States. &nbsp;Courses are registered as if taken at Muhlenberg and grades are calculated in the GPA. For additional information see the Campus Coordinator: Dr. Donna Kish-Goodling.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#w1212" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="w1212">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="w121">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          WESCOE SCHOOL OF MUHLENBERG COLLEGE 
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="w1212" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="w121">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">The mission of The Wescoe School of Muhlenberg College is to provide lifelong learners the opportunity to continue and enhance their education and to do so in ways that recognize their experience, maturity, motivation, life circumstances, and capacity for independent scholarship.</p>
<p align="justify">Lifelong learners are very different from traditionally aged full-time students. Recognizing this, the Wescoe School offers innovative programs of study with distinct and specialized opportunities. Its students can complete a degree by enrolling in classes at night, during the day (on a limited basis), and on weekends.</p>
<p class="underline">Accelerated Programs</p>
<p align="justify">The Wescoe School offers the Bachelor's degree in an accelerated format for the following majors: Business Administration; Business Administration with concentration areas in Healthcare Management, Human Resources Leadership, Financial Services, and Supply Chain Management; and Information Systems. &nbsp;Students learn collaboratively in a feedback-intensive program that prepares them for leadership in their chosen field and graduate level academic study. The curriculum is designed for immediate application to the workplace and develops presentation, facilitation, and problem-solving skills.</p>
<p align="justify">Students in this program complete 17 modules of study in a team-based experiential learning environment. They attend one four-hour class each week and meet outside of class for a weekly three- to four-hour session during which they work together on team projects and presentations. The program concludes with a culminating capstone project. This project is completed in cooperation with a local not-for- or for-profit organization whereby the students act as a consulting group to the organization. The students then present their findings to a panel of their instructors.&nbsp;</p>
<p class="underline">Liberal Arts Programs</p>
<p align="justify">Adult students have the option to enroll for credit classes in several formats: the traditional 15-week program, 8-week sessions, or weekend sessions. <span class="italic">The 8-week and weekend sessions are available only to Wescoe students and incorporate pedagogical practices appropriate to this population.</span> Under special circumstances, students with senior status may petition the Dean of Academic Life to be allowed to register one course unit in an 8-week or weekend session.</p>
<p align="justify">Day students may register in courses offered through the Wescoe School 15-week session during the add/drop period on a space-available basis with permission from the appropriate department chair and the Dean of the Wescoe School. No more than one such course may be registered in any one semester and should be done only after consultation with the student's academic advisor. First-year students must obtain signed permission from the Dean of Academic Life prior to consideration of the request by the Dean of the Wescoe School.</p>
<p align="justify">Additionally, the Wescoe School offers major certificates in every major of the College. Many Wescoe students take courses to prepare for future graduate study or to upgrade or learn new skills. In addition to the Bachelor's degree, Wescoe students may earn the Associate of Arts degree in some majors or enroll in a non-credit enrichment course.</p>
<p class="underline">Summer Study</p>
<p align="justify">Muhlenberg College offers a variety of day and evening courses during a series of summer sessions. These courses, while typically offered in an accelerated format, are unlike the courses in other 8-week and weekend sessions because they incorporate pedagogy appropriate for full-time undergraduate students. All course units and grades earned through summer study at Muhlenberg are attributed to the total program of the student and influence the cumulative grade point average and academic standing of the student accordingly. Summer load is 2 courses at a time for a maximum combined summer load of 4 course units. &nbsp;Summer study materials are available through the Wescoe School in early March.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1212" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1212">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="121">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          WITHDRAWAL FROM A COURSE
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1212" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="121">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">A student may withdraw from a course after the add/drop period until the end of the 45<sup>th</sup> class day with the approval of his or her academic advisor. The student must process a withdrawal form, available from and returned to the Office of the Registrar, by the deadline. Both the instructor of the course and the student's advisor must sign the form. A "W" grade will be assigned indicating that the student has withdrawn from the course. The last day to withdraw is identified each semester on the College's academic calendar.</p>
<p align="justify">A full-time student seeking to withdraw from a course or courses so that s/he will earn fewer than 3 course units, must consult with his/her academic advisor concerning such a withdrawal. The advisor then consults with the Dean of Academic Life. If the Dean approves the withdrawal, s/he will forward the completed withdrawal form to the Office of the Registrar for processing.</p>
<p align="justify">No course may be withdrawn after the 45<sup>th</sup> class day except for documented medical reasons certified by the Executive Director of Health and Counseling Services.</p>
<p align="justify">A student who attends a different section of a course than the section registered must make the correction to his/her schedule by dropping the course online or processing a withdrawal form. Students who fail to correct registration errors or officially drop will receive a failing grade (F).</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1232" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1232">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="123">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          WITHDRAWAL FROM MUHLENBERG COLLEGE
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1232" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="123">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">A student who wishes to officially withdraw from the College must notify the Office of the Registrar. A student must complete withdrawal procedures prior to the beginning of the first semester in which he or she is not enrolled to ensure that the academic record will accurately reflect his or her intentions. All financial obligations must be satisfied before an official withdrawal can be granted or the academic record can be released. At the time of withdrawal, the student's BergID card will be inactivated.</p>
<p align="justify">Students who have been charged with a disciplinary infraction but who have not yet completed the Judicial process, will be unable to Withdraw from Muhlenberg until the Judicial process is complete.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div><div class="panel panel-default">
  <a data-toggle="collapse" 
     data-parent="#collapse-accordion" 
     href="#1242" 
     aria-expanded="false" 
     aria-controls="1242">
  	<div class="panel-heading" 
       role="tab" 
       id="124">
      <p class="panel-title pull-left">
          WRITING PROGRAM
  </p>
      <p class="panel-title pull-right">
        
            <span class='fa fa-plus-square-o' ></span>
      </p>	
       


      <div class="clearfix"></div>
  	</div>
  </a>
  <div id="1242" 
       class="panel-collapse collapse" 
       role="tabpanel" 
       aria-labelledby="124">
    <div class="panel-body">
        <p align="justify">Muhlenberg College offers cross-curricular writing programs in which faculty from every department participate. In specially designated writing-intensive courses, students attend to writing in context - within particular disciplines - but also with attention to ways in which effective writing shares similar traits across the disciplines. The aim of the program is to equip students to write analytically in a variety of writing situations.</p>
<p align="justify">The basic premise of the writing program is that writing is necessary to thinking and learning; it is an essential way of acquiring knowledge and of arriving at ideas about it. &nbsp;Another primary assumption of the program is that the ability to write well is not a skill one can acquire in a semester of grammar study. Instead, students are encouraged to take a number of writing-intensive courses throughout their careers at the College. The Writing Program is supported by a Writing Center that is staffed by trained peer tutors with majors in a wide range of disciplines.</p>
<p align="justify">A writing-intensive course is a regular academic course in which enrollment is limited to twenty students, and students will complete a minimum of fifteen pages of writing broken into at least three assignments. One of these assignments must be a revision in response to the instructor's written comments. As a requirement for graduation, students are required to take a minimum of three writing-intensive (W) courses - one First-Year Seminar, one W-course selected from anywhere in the curriculum, and one W-course designated by the student's major.</p>
<p align="justify">In exceptional cases, students may appeal to the Writing Program Committee to receive special W-credit for a course that is not designated as a W. The fact that a student has done a significant amount of writing in a course is not, of itself, sufficient reason for assigning special W-credit, since a writing-intensive course is a particular kind of collaborative learning experience.</p>
<p align="justify">For questions or additional information see Dr. Jill Stephen or Dr. David Rosenwasser, Department of English.</p>
    </div>
  </div>
</div>
    
  </div>
